  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (No new smoke; existing tests cover the regression.)
- **2026-04-28 — vector compound assign on non-Identifier lvalues (real bug)**: vector `arr[i] += rhs`, `s.m += rhs`, `*p += rhs` for `__attribute__((vector_size))` types failed: Index fell through `_compound_assign`'s vector branch (Identifier-only) into the generic 32-bit path which tried to load 16 bytes into EAX and raised. Member with vector type used the existing Member-vector branch which still had double-eval of the lvalue.
  - **Fix**: dispatch all non-Identifier vector lvalues to a new `_compound_assign_vector_lvalue` that uses the same hidden-snapshot pattern as the LL/int128 fixes. Hidden 4-byte addr slot + N-byte snapshot slot. Compute &lvalue once into addr, copy current bytes into snapshot, synthesize `Identifier(snap_slot) OP rhs`, evaluate via `_vector_value_address` into a result temp, then copy back to *addr_slot.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (348 total).
- **2026-04-28 — _Complex compound + struct/array init for complex members (real bug)**:
  - **Complex compound assign on any lvalue**: `c += rhs` for `_Complex T` types fell through to the generic 32-bit path, which then evaluated `rhs` as int — failing for complex BinaryOp like `10.0+20.0i`. Added a dispatch in `_compound_assign` that routes ComplexType lvalues to a new `_compound_assign_complex_lvalue`. Identifier path desugars trivially through `_complex_copy_assign(BinaryOp("=", lhs, BinaryOp(op, lhs, rhs)))`. Non-Identifier path uses the snapshot pattern: hidden 4-byte addr + N-byte snap slots, compute &lhs once, copy to snap, synthesize `Identifier(snap) OP rhs`, route through `_complex_copy_assign` with a synthetic `*addr_id` lvalue.
  - **Complex struct member init**: `struct S { _Complex double v; }; struct S s = {1.0+2.0i};` — `_struct_init` had branches for float / long-long / int128 members but not complex, falling through to `_eval_expr_to_eax` which fails for complex BinaryOp. Added a complex-member branch that emits `&dest` on the stack and evaluates the complex expression directly into the destination via `_eval_complex_into_top`.
  - **Complex array element init**: `_Complex double arr[2] = {1.0+2.0i, 3.0+4.0i};` — same pattern in `_array_init`.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (349 total).
- **2026-04-28 — clear error for ++/-- on _Complex Identifier**: previously crashed with `KeyError: 16` because `_inc_dec`'s width-table only has entries for 1/2/4 bytes. Now raises a clear "++ on _Complex operand X not supported" with a hint to use `__real__ x ++`. The behavior was never well-defined (gcc accepts `++ complex` and increments the real part — non-standard and rarely used) and properly supporting it would need more plumbing than the test suites need.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (No new smoke; this is an error-path improvement only.)
- **2026-04-28 — scope-aware `_collect_call_temps`**: `for (int i=0;...) ... for (u128 i=0;...) total += i;` failed at codegen time with `can't take address of __int128 UnaryOp` for the second loop's `i++`. Root cause: `_collect_call_temps` walked the body via `_walk_ast` (a flat dataclass-fields recursion) and pre-filled a SINGLE flat dict of `name → type` from each VarDecl. Two VarDecls of `i` collided on the dedupe-by-name (`if sub.name not in ctx.slots[-1]`) so the second binding was dropped. When the inner BinaryOp/UnaryOp dispatch then queried `_type_of(Identifier("i"))` to decide whether the result was int128, it got the first decl's `int` and skipped the temp allocation. Fix: rewrote the walker to be scope-aware, mirroring `_collect_locals`'s structure — `CompoundStmt` and `ForStmt` push their own scopes, `VarDecl` registers in the current scope before recursing into its init. Per-node temp allocation (now `_collect_call_temps_node`) is unchanged; it just runs in the right scope. Same fix protects `_resolve_typeof_in_body`-like sites that *aren't* yet scope-aware, but those are out of scope for this slice.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (350 total).
- **2026-04-28 — long-long bit-field compound assign: address-once snapshot (real bug)**: `arr[i++].bf += rhs` for a long-long-storage bit-field used to fire `i++` twice. `_compound_assign_bitfield_ll` synthesized `inner = lvalue OP rhs` and called `_bitfield_store_ll_simple(expr.left, bf, inner, ctx)` which (1) computed `&storage_unit` via `_member_address(expr, ctx)` — first eval of `arr[i++]` — and (2) called `_eval_expr_to_edx_eax(inner, ctx)`, where `inner` contained `expr.left` again as the BinaryOp's left, triggering a second eval of `arr[i++]`. Same shape as the LL/int128/vector compound assign bugs from earlier — fix was the snapshot pattern: alloc `addr_slot` (4 B, pointer) and `snap_slot` (8 B, long long); compute `&storage_unit` once and save in addr_slot; read the storage unit, extract the bit-field value (shift-right by `bit_offset`, mask to `bit_width`, sign-extend if signed); save in snap_slot; synthesize `Identifier(snap_name) OP rhs` and route through the LL ladder; mask + position the result; RMW `[addr_slot]` clearing the field bits and OR'ing in the new positioned value. `_bitfield_store_ll_simple` is unchanged (still used by direct LL bit-field assignments). Verified with side-effect tests across signed/unsigned, all op kinds (`+= -= *= /= %= <<= >>= &= |= ^=`), and mixed bit-fields sharing storage units. 1 new smoke test; 351 total.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (351 total).
- **2026-04-28 — long-long bit-field ++/--: dispatch + address-once (real bug)**: `arr[i++].bf++` for a long-long-storage bit-field used to error out at codegen with "long-long bit-field ++/-- not yet supported". `_inc_dec_lvalue` always dispatched Member operands to `_inc_dec_bitfield`, which rejected `unit_size == 8`. The companion `_inc_dec_bitfield_ll` already existed but was only wired up from `_inc_dec_ll` (long-long Identifier path) — the lvalue path never reached it. Even when reached, `_inc_dec_bitfield_ll` had a triple-eval bug: `_bitfield_load_ll(expr.operand, bf, ctx)` evaluated `arr[i++]` once, then `_bitfield_store_ll_simple(expr.operand, bf, BinaryOp(+, expr.operand, 1), ctx)` evaluated it twice more (once for the store address, once for the read inside the inner BinaryOp). Two fixes in one slice: (1) `_inc_dec_lvalue` now routes long-long bit-fields to `_inc_dec_bitfield_ll`. (2) Rewrote `_inc_dec_bitfield_ll` with the address-once snapshot pattern — compute `&storage_unit` once, save in addr_slot; extract the current value into snap_slot; bump (`add eax, 1; adc edx, 0` or `sub eax, 1; sbb edx, 0`); mask + position the new value; RMW `[addr_slot]`. Postfix yields snap_slot's value; prefix re-loads via a new `_bitfield_load_ll_via_addr` helper. Verified with pre/post-increment, signed/unsigned, varying widths (24/33/40), and side-effect-bearing array indices.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (352 total).
- **2026-04-28 — clear errors for ++/-- on _Complex / vector lvalues**: previous slice gave a clear error for `++c` (Identifier) but `arr[i]++` / `s.cv++` / `*pc++` for _Complex lvalues still crashed with `KeyError: 16` because `_inc_dec_lvalue`'s width-table is `{1: byte, 2: word, 4: dword}` and `_size_of(_Complex double) == 16`. Vector lvalue ++/-- had the same shape (size 16/8/4 depending on vector). Both now raise a clear "++ on _Complex/vector lvalue not supported" before the width lookup. (int128 ++/-- on lvalues is already handled correctly via the int128 dispatch in `_eval_expr_to_eax` — it never reaches `_inc_dec_lvalue` because the int128-typed expression is intercepted by `_int128_value_address` first.)

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (Error-path improvement only; no new smoke.)
- **2026-04-28 — complex division: imag part divides wrong direction (real bug)**: `_complex_div_into_top` was emitting `fdivp st1, st0` for the imag-numerator division — that computes `st1 / st0`, i.e. `denom / numer_imag`, the wrong direction. The real part used `fdiv st0, st1` (no pop) which correctly computed `numer_real / denom`, so only imag was broken. Concrete repro: `(1.0+0.0i) / (1.0+1.0i)` produced `0.5 + -2.0i` instead of `0.5 - 0.5i`. Fix: switch to `fdivrp st1, st0` (note the `r` for reverse-divide), which computes `st0 / st1` and pops, yielding `numer_imag / denom`. The torture suite didn't catch this because none of its complex-division tests have `__imag__ != 0` in the result. Verified across `_Complex float` / `_Complex double` / `_Complex long double`, signed and unsigned cases. The bug has been latent since the `_Complex` arithmetic slice landed in 2026-04-26.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (353 total).
- **2026-04-28 — `!complex_var` / `!int128_var` crash (real bug)**: `_unary` evaluated the operand into EAX UNCONDITIONALLY before checking the op (line `out = self._eval_expr_to_eax(expr.operand, ctx)`). For `+`/`-`/`~` the result was used; for `!` the eval was discarded and re-done via `_eval_to_bool_eax`. But the upfront eval failed for any operand that doesn't fit a single EAX load — `_Complex double` (16 B), `__int128` (16 B), `_Complex float` (8 B), etc. — with "can't load size-{N} value into eax". Fix: dispatch `!` first, before the EAX-load. The op-specific path goes straight to `_eval_to_bool_eax` (which knows about complex / int128 / vector / float / int) without an unnecessary intermediate load.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (354 total).
- **2026-04-28 — bare `__int128` keyword + int128→int cast chain (two real bugs)**: two related gaps in __int128 support, both unexercised by the suites because they all use `unsigned __int128` everywhere. (1) `__int128 x = ...;` (without signed/unsigned modifier) failed at the parser with "Expected SEMICOLON" — uc_core's `_is_declaration_start` and `_is_type_name` treated `__int128`/`__int128_t`/`__uint128_t` as plain IDENTIFIERs (not type-introducing). `unsigned __int128` worked only because the leading `unsigned` keyword tripped TYPE_SPECIFIER detection first. Fixed both predicates to recognize the bare keyword. (2) `(int)(long long)((__int128)0x100 << 16)` produced garbage (got `0x10fffd4` instead of `0x1000000`). `_eval_expr_to_eax` for an int128-typed expression returns the value's ADDRESS in EAX (since 16 B doesn't fit a register), but `_cast(target=long long)` and the further `_cast(target=int)` just passed the address through unchanged. The int128 → long long path in `_eval_expr_to_edx_eax(Cast)` was correct (loads `[ecx]`/`[ecx+4]`), but the EAX-only path in `_cast` was missing a load. Fix: in `_cast`, when src is int128, dispatch via `_int128_value_address` and load through the address (low 4 bytes for int / pointer / long long target; load + narrow for char/short).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +2 smoke tests (356 total).
- **2026-04-28 — `WATCOM_FLAT32` missing double_size override (real bug)**: `sizeof(double)` constant-folded to 4 instead of 8. uc_core's `WATCOM_FLAT32` TypeConfig didn't override `double_size`, so it took the TypeConfig default of `double_size=4` (defaults are sized for the Z80 baseline). uc_core's optimizer constant-folds `sizeof(double)` via `type_config.sizeof_basic("double")` early in the pipeline, baking in the wrong value before uc386's codegen ever sees it. uc386's `_BASIC_SIZES["double"] = 8` was correct for cases that flowed through codegen's own size paths (e.g. `sizeof(double_var)` via `_type_of(expr)`), but the constant-folded path landed in the asm as `mov eax, 4`. Fix: `WATCOM_FLAT32` now explicitly sets `float_size=4, double_size=8, long_double_size=8` to match uc386's codegen. The torture / c-testsuite suites didn't catch this because none of their tests do `if (sizeof(double) != 8) abort();` (they happily use a `double_var` instead, which goes through the correct codegen path). +1 smoke test. uc_core change committed separately.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (357 total).
- **2026-04-28 — wide string sizeof returns byte count (real bug)**: `sizeof(L"hi")` returned 3 instead of 6. uc_core's optimizer folded `sizeof(StringLiteral)` to `len(value) + 1` regardless of `is_wide`. For wide strings, the byte count needs to scale by `sizeof(wchar_t)`. Fix: in uc_core, skip the fold for wide strings (return SizeofExpr unchanged); in uc386 codegen, recognize wide-string SizeofExpr in both `_const_eval` and `_eval_expr_to_eax` paths and emit `(len + 1) * 2` (uc386 uses `__WCHAR_TYPE__=unsigned short`). uc_core change committed separately.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (358 total).
- **2026-04-28 — printf precision for integer formats (real bug)**: `printf("%.3d", 42)` produced `42` instead of `042`. The dos_emu printf parsed the precision but only applied it to `%s` (truncate). For integer formats `%d/%i/%u/%x/%X/%o`, precision specifies the MINIMUM number of digits — the value is left-padded with zeros to reach that count. Per C99 7.21.6.1#5, when precision is specified the `0` flag is ignored, and "the result of converting a zero value with a precision of zero is no characters" (so `printf("[%.0d]", 0)` should give `[]`). Fix: split the integer formatting into "build digits" + "apply precision (zero-pad digits)" + "apply width (space-pad whole)" steps. Sign-aware: zero pad goes between the sign and the digits when both `0` flag and width apply. Special case for the val==0 with precision==0 case. Same for u/x/X/o (where `prefix` plays the role of `sign`). Verified across `%.3d` / `%.0d` / `%.5x` / `%#08x` / `%05d` (with negatives) / `%+5d` (positive with plus flag) / `%10.5d` (combined width and precision).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (No new smoke; printf is exercised via dos_emu, not directly testable from asm.)
- **2026-04-28 — printf float zero-pad + sign flags (real bug)**: `printf("%010.2f", 3.14)` produced `      3.14` (space pad) instead of `0000003.14` (zero pad). The float branch ignored `zero_pad`, `plus_flag`, and `space_flag`. Also missing: capital `%E` / `%G` aliases. Fix: after Python-level formatting, prepend `+`/space sign for positives if requested; in width-padding, zero-pad goes between the sign (if any) and the digits, otherwise space-pad. Added `b"E"` and `b"G"` to the conversion set so they don't fall through to the unknown-format branch. Verified across `%g` / `%e` / `%+f` / `%010.2f` (positive and negative) / `% f`.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (No new smoke; printf is exercised via dos_emu.)
- **2026-04-28 — printf `*` width and precision (real bug)**: `printf("%*d", 5, 42)` and `printf("%.*d", 5, 42)` weren't supported — the format parser only consumed integer-literal width/precision. Per C99, `*` reads the value from the next `va_arg` (as `int`); a negative width is equivalent to the `-` left-align flag plus the absolute width. Also lifted the `read32_le`/`read64_le`/`ap_box` init from inside the per-spec loop to the top of the `_printf_format` function so the new `*` branches can advance `ap_box` during format-spec parsing (before the conv letter is read). Removed the redundant `ap = ap_box[0]` at the bottom of the loop since ap_box now persists across iterations. Verified `%*d` / `%.*d` / `%*.*d`.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (No new smoke; printf is exercised via dos_emu.)
- **2026-04-28 — printf `%n` (real bug)**: `printf("hello%n", &n)` fell through to the unknown-format branch, outputting `%n` literally and not writing to the pointer. C99's `%n` writes the count of characters output so far to the `int*` argument. Length modifiers `%hn` / `%hhn` / `%lln` select narrower stores. Added handling. (Note: glibc has historically deprecated `%n` for security reasons in format-string attacks, but it's part of the standard and several torture/c-testsuite tests would use it.)

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. (No new smoke; printf is exercised via dos_emu.)
- **2026-04-28 — non-consecutive multi-level designators + array-index outer + `x*2 → x+x` w/ side effects (4 real bugs)**: probing for latent bugs surfaced four:
  - **Global struct multi-level designator path didn't merge.** `struct Outer g = { .s.a = 11, .s.c = 33, .x = 99 };` errored out with "only single-level `.field` designators supported" because `_emit_global_struct_init` had no merging step (only the local `_struct_init` had `_merge_nested_designators`). Fix: call `_merge_nested_designators` on `init.values` early in the global path, before any single-level designator dispatch.
  - **Non-consecutive same-outer multi-level designators clobber each other.** `{ .s.a = 11, .extra = 99, .s.b = 22 }` previously split into TWO `.s = {...}` slot writes, where the second's recursive emit zero-filled `.s.a` (because `_struct_init`/`_emit_global_struct_init` for `.s` would fully zero unfilled members). Two-part fix: (1) `_merge_nested_designators` now scans ALL prior entries (not just `out[-1]`) for a same-outer synthesized InitializerList and appends the new inner designator there, consolidating the run at the FIRST source position; (2) for `_emit_global_struct_init`'s slot_values dict, when the slot already holds an InitializerList and the new value is also an InitializerList, concatenate their values rather than overwriting (defensive — paired with the merge consolidation but harmless if the consolidation happens first).
  - **Array-index outer wasn't recognized in merging.** `{ [0].a = 1, [0].b = 2 }` for an array of struct errored at `_array_init` / `_emit_global_array_init` with "only single-level integer designators supported". `_merge_nested_designators` only matched `str` outer designators; it now also matches `IntLiteral` outers via a new `outer_key()` helper, returning `("name", str)` or `("idx", int)`. `_array_init` and `_emit_global_array_init` now both call `_merge_nested_designators` on their iter_values.
  - **`(n += 5) * 2` got strength-reduced to `(n += 5) + (n += 5)`** — duplicating the side-effect-bearing operand. The optimizer's `_strength_reduce_mul` rule for `x * 2 → x + x` (saving an `imul` on Z80 — single ADD HL,HL) didn't gate on side-effects. Added `not self._expr_has_side_effects(other)` to the shift==1 branch. Other shift values (4, 8, 16) only emit the operand once via `<<`, so they're already safe.

  4 new smoke tests covering each path; no new tests for the optimizer fix beyond a structural assertion (count of `mov [ebp - 4], eax` stays at 2 — init + the one `+= 5`). Verified via lots of hand-crafted probes including chained struct+array MD designators, MD with side-effect-bearing values, MD with bit-fields / floats / long-long / int128 members, deeply nested MD, repeat-same-path MD (last-write-wins), MD in compound literals, MD in unions, anonymous struct member designators.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 363/363 (4 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — int128 negation flag-clobber + global pointer init via `_resolve_static_addr` (2 real bugs)**: more probing surfaced two:
  - **`-(__int128)1` produced wrong high bits.** `_unary_int128`'s negation loop emitted `xor eax, eax` between consecutive `sbb` instructions to zero EAX. But `xor` clears the carry/borrow flag (along with ZF, SF, etc.), breaking the borrow propagation across dwords. Concrete repro: `-(__int128)1` should give 0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF; we got `0x00000000_00000000_00000000_FFFFFFFF` because dwords 1, 2, 3 each saw borrow=0 instead of borrow=1. Fix: replace the inter-iteration `xor eax, eax` with `mov eax, 0` (which doesn't affect flags). The initial `xor` before the first `sub` is fine — that one isn't expected to preserve any prior flag. The bug had been latent since the int128 implementation landed; torture didn't catch it because no test negated an int128 with non-zero low bits and zero high bits in a way that exposed the high-byte clearing.
  - **Global `int *p = arr + N`, `&arr[0] + N`, etc.** previously failed at `_const_eval` ("got Identifier `arr`") because `_emit_global_init`'s pointer-init path only recognized `&<lvalue>` chains, not bare-name array decay or other address-arithmetic forms. Fix: for pointer-typed globals, dispatch through `_resolve_static_addr` directly — that walker already handles arrays, `&...`, `[N]`, `.m`, `*p` chains, and pointer arithmetic. Also added a missing `UnaryOp("&")` case to `_resolve_static_addr` itself: the walker is already producing addresses of l-value chains, so `&` should be a no-op (it just re-anchors at the operand). Without this case, `&arr[0] + N` (an explicit-`&` form) was failing the resolution.
  - **Side bug in the same probe: `int *r = q + 2` where `q` is a pointer-typed global** was silently producing `dd _q + 8` — but at runtime `q + 2` reads `q`'s value and adds 8, NOT the variable's address. Fix: in `_resolve_static_addr`'s BinaryOp branch, gate the resolution on `_decays_to_static(e)` — only an array name, function name, string literal, `&...` chain, `[N]`/`.m` chain, or recursive pointer-arithmetic on those decays to a static address. A bare pointer-typed Identifier represents a runtime read, not a static address. Pointer-typed globals now correctly fall through to `_const_eval` which raises a clear error (you can't statically initialize from a runtime pointer value).

  3 new smoke tests; lots of hand-crafted probes covering the bugs and adjacent corners. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 365/365 (3 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — typeof in declarator + complex via fnptr + strstr (3 real bugs)**: more probing surfaced three:
  - **`typeof(x) y = ...;`** at function scope was rejected with "unsupported type ... TypeofType" because `_check_supported_type` (called inside `_collect_locals`) saw the bare `TypeofType` AST node before the resolver ran. The resolver was scheduled AFTER `_collect_locals`, so any decl whose declared type was itself a `TypeofType` failed up front. Fix: move `_resolve_typeof_in_body` BEFORE `_collect_locals`, and rewrite it to build its `flat_types` map directly from each VarDecl's `var_type` AST field (since `ctx.decl_types` is empty pre-`_collect_locals`).
  - **`typeof(arr[0]) elem = ...;`, `typeof(s.x) tx = ...;`, `typeof(&s.x) pp = ...;`, `typeof(s.x + s.x) tsum = ...;`** all failed even after the move because the resolver only recognized bare Identifier operands. Extended `resolve_inner` to handle Index (returns element type), Member (resolves through struct layout), `*p` (returns pointee), `&x` (returns pointer-to), Cast (returns target_type), BinaryOp (approximates usual arithmetic conversion — wider operand wins; comparison/logical ops yield int), UnaryOp (propagates operand's type), and TernaryOp (uses true branch). Globals/extern vars/function-name Identifiers fall through to live `_type_of`.
  - **`cfn_t fn = dbl; fn(c);`** (calling a `_Complex T (*)(...)` via function pointer) raised "can't take address of complex `Call`" because `_is_complex_returning_call` used `_call_target` which only matched direct calls (Identifier callee in `_func_return_types`). Indirect calls returned `target=None` so the predicate returned False, the call wasn't recognized as complex-returning, no per-call retptr temp was reserved, and `_complex_value_address(Call)` then tried to take the address of the non-temp result. Fix: switch to `_call_return_type` which already walks function-pointer types for indirect calls; `isinstance(rt, ast.ComplexType)` then catches both forms uniformly.
  - **`strstr` was missing from libc.** Added a naive O(n*m) byte-by-byte search in i386_dos_libc.asm. Empty needle returns haystack per C99 7.21.5.7. Used by enough adjacent probe paths to be worth having even though the suites don't reference it directly.

  No new smoke tests for these — all three were caught by hand-crafted probe files (`probe_typedef_fnptr_int.c`, `probe_typeof_extras.c`, `probe_complex_in_callback.c`) and verified end-to-end at runtime under dos_emu. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 365/365. Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — typedef of `__int128 (*fnptr)(...)` + ternary type per UAC (2 real bugs)**:
  - **`typedef __int128 (*ifn_t)(int);`** raised "Expected SEMICOLON" at the typedef line. Root cause: uc_core's `_parse_declaration` has a K&R-style implicit-int extension that peeks past any IDENTIFIER followed by `(`/`;`/`=`/`,` and synthesizes `int` as the base type. Since `__int128` tokenizes as IDENTIFIER and is followed by `(`, the extension fired and treated `__int128` as a function name being declared with implicit-int return type. Fix: exclude `__int128` / `__int128_t` / `__uint128_t` from the implicit-int peek so they fall through to `_parse_type_specifier` (which already recognizes them as type specifiers via the IDENTIFIER fallback at lines 552-571).
  - **`sizeof(1 ? (char)1 : (int)1)` returned 1 instead of 4.** Per C99 6.5.15#5, the result type of `cond ? a : b` is determined by the usual arithmetic conversions of both arms — independent of which arm runtime selects. uc386's `_type_of(TernaryOp)` was just `return _type_of(true_expr)`, so for arms with different ranks (char vs int, int vs long long, int vs double, etc.) it picked the wrong size. Fix: apply UAC to both arm types — float wins (via `_float_promotion`), then int128, then long long, then pointer, then unsigned-vs-signed default. Verified across all combinations (`char/short/int/long/long long`, `int/float/double`, `pointer/null`, `signed/unsigned`).

  2 new smoke tests covering each bug; lots of hand-crafted probes (probe_typedef_int128_fnptr.c, probe_sizeof_expr.c, probe_ternary_types.c). **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 367/367 (2 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — `_Bool` normalization across all paths (multiple real bugs)**: per C 6.3.1.2, any conversion to `_Bool` produces 0 (if source compares equal to 0) or 1 (otherwise). uc386 was storing raw values into 1-byte bool slots, so `_Bool b = 5; if (b != 1) abort();` aborted because the slot held 5. Found and fixed across every path that produces a bool value:
  - **`_store_from_eax(addr, ty)`** for bool target: emits `test eax, eax; setne al; movzx eax, al; mov [...], al`. Catches `_Bool b = expr;` and chained `_Bool` assignments.
  - **`_emit_global_init(BasicType("bool"))`**: const-fold the value to 1 if non-zero, 0 if zero. Also catches NASM truncation surprise where `db 256` lays down 0.
  - **`_emit_global_array_init` for bool elements**: same const-fold per element. Without this, `_Bool g[5] = {5, 0, 256, ...};` laid down `db 5, 0, 0, ...`.
  - **`_inc_dec(Identifier(bool))`**: `b++` was `inc byte [...]` which from 1 produced 2 in the slot. Now load + add 1 + bool-store, with prefix/postfix value semantics preserved.
  - **`_inc_dec_lvalue` for `arr[i]++` / `s.m++` / `*p++`** when target is `_Bool`: same address-once pattern with bool-store.
  - **`_cast` to `_Bool`**: routes through `_eval_to_bool_eax` (which handles long-long / float / int128 / complex / int / pointer sources via existing logic) plus explicit `test+setne+movzx` to ensure EAX is 0/1 even for int sources where `_eval_to_bool_eax` doesn't normalize on its own.
  - **`_emit_call` arg coercion** for `_Bool` expected param with non-bool int arg: normalize via `_eval_to_bool_eax` + setne + push, so the callee's byte-load reads 0 or 1.
  - **`_return` for `_Bool`-returning functions**: same source-aware normalization path so a callee `return 5;` produces EAX=1.
  - Removed the int128/long-long/float/complex inline branches from `_cast` since they're now covered by the generic `_eval_to_bool_eax` dispatch.

  None of the reference suites (1514/1514 torture, 220/220 c-testsuite) exercise these paths — `_Bool` is rarely tested directly, and the existing tests all use `b = comparison_result` which already produces 0/1. 6 new smoke tests + lots of hand-crafted probes covering all paths (cast from int/long-long/int128/float/complex/pointer; assign; ++/-- on Identifier and lvalue; struct/array/union init; param/return; global init). **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 373/373 (6 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — struct/complex/vector ternary + complex-int arithmetic via int ops (multiple real bugs)**: probing surfaced several major gaps. Aggregate types in ternary arms had never been wired up — the suites never write `cond ? struct_a : struct_b` style code, so the missing dispatch was latent.
  - **Struct ternary (`cond ? sa : sb`).** `_struct_address` had no `TernaryOp` branch — fell through to the generic "can't take address of TernaryOp for `.member`" error. Added per-ternary temp allocation in `_collect_call_temps_node` for `TernaryOp` whose result is `StructType`, plus a new `_struct_ternary_into(expr, dest_disp, ty, ctx)` that emits the conditional dispatch: eval condition via `_eval_to_bool_eax`, `test`/`jz` to false_label, `_struct_address(true_expr)` + memcpy into dest, `jmp end`, false_label, `_struct_address(false_expr)` + memcpy into dest, end_label. Returns `&dest` in EAX so callers (`.member`, var-init, struct-arg copy) chain naturally. Both arms must produce the same struct layout per C; the temp size matches the declared struct.
  - **Complex ternary (`cond ? ca : cb`).** Same shape: `_complex_value_address(TernaryOp)` had no branch. New `_complex_ternary_into` allocates a complex-sized temp via the existing `_collect_call_temps_node` complex path (which already covered `TernaryOp` via the catch-all `(BinaryOp, UnaryOp, Cast, TernaryOp)` predicate at line 3467), then conditionally evaluates each arm into the dest via `_eval_complex_to`. The standard complex eval pipeline handles all arm shapes uniformly: lvalue / Call / arithmetic BinaryOp / Compound / nested ternary.
  - **Complex ternary INSIDE a complex BinaryOp arm.** `_eval_complex_into_top` had no `TernaryOp` branch and fell through to `_scalar_to_complex_into_top` (the "real-valued expression promoted to complex" fallback), which then called `_eval_float_to_st0(TernaryOp)` → `_eval_expr_to_eax(TernaryOp)` → `_ternary` → `_binary` of a complex add → `_add_sub` → `_eval_expr_to_eax(imaginary FloatLiteral)` → "expression FloatLiteral not implemented yet". Concrete repro: `(n > 10) ? (1.0 + 1.0i) : ((n > 0) ? (2.0 + 2.0i) : (3.0 + 3.0i))`. Added a TernaryOp branch to `_eval_complex_into_top` that emits the conditional jump and recurses each arm via `_eval_complex_into_top` itself (the dest address sits at TOS across the recursive calls per the helper's contract, so no stack management needed). Distinct labels (`cplx_into_tern_*`) from the outer `_complex_ternary_into` ones (`cplx_tern_*`) so nesting works without name collisions.
  - **`__real__ (cond ? a : b)` and `__imag__ (cond ? a : b)`.** `_complex_part_address` only recognized lvalues / Calls as operands; complex sub-expressions (BinaryOp/UnaryOp/Cast/TernaryOp/imaginary FloatLiteral) raised "operand must be a simple lvalue". Refactored to fall through to `_complex_value_address` for any node that has a pre-allocated temp slot — that helper already handles the full set, so all paths flow uniformly.
  - **Vector ternary.** `_vector_value_address` had no `TernaryOp` branch — raised "vector value: unsupported expression TernaryOp". Added `_vector_ternary_into` (memcpy-based, mirrors struct ternary) plus per-ternary temp allocation for vector-typed `TernaryOp` in `_collect_call_temps_node`.
  - **Complex int arithmetic via integer ops (not FPU).** `_Complex int * _Complex int` was producing `0 + 0i` because `_eval_complex_into_top` routes `+`/`-`/`*` through `_complex_addsub_into_top` / `_complex_mul_into_top`, which `fld` the halves as IEEE-754 floats. Loading `0x00000004` as a float gives a denormal (~5.6e-45); multiplying two denormals underflows to zero. Even add/sub only worked for very small int values where the bit pattern happens to look like a usable float. Fix: in `_eval_complex_into_top`'s BinaryOp branch, when `eff_ty.base_type` is in `_COMPLEX_INT_BASES` (char/short/int/long/long long) and half size is 1/2/4 and op is `+`/`-`/`*`, dispatch to a new `_complex_int_arith_into_top` that loads halves as integers (movsx/movzx for sub-word, mov for 4-byte) and applies `add`/`sub`/`imul`. The schoolbook complex multiply needs four imul partials (ar*br, ai*bi, ar*bi, ai*br) — implemented in `_complex_int_mul_into_top_simple` with stack scratch for both operands so we can revisit the partials without re-running side effects. The const-eval path at `_const_eval_complex` already handles the "both operands are constant" case for int complex; this path covers runtime args.

  Verified end-to-end across many probe shapes: struct ternary with function-call arms (only chosen arm's call fires), nested ternaries (struct/complex/vector/int128/long long arms), complex ternary with arithmetic arms (`(1+2i) + (3+4i)`), complex ternary as compound-assign rhs / function arg / function return value, vector ternary as function arg / return, int128 ternary as arg / return, char/short/long-long/_Bool/pointer/nullptr/mixed-precision ternary, `__real__`/`__imag__` of any complex sub-expression including ternary. 4 new smoke tests targeting the canonical asm patterns. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 377/377 (4 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — _Generic, ptr+LL, ll-context, fnptr-deref, anon-union init (6 real bugs)**: more probing surfaced six unrelated correctness bugs.
  - **`_types_equal` missing ComplexType branch.** `_Generic((cd), _Complex double: 1, default: 2)` always picked default because `_types_equal(ComplexType, ComplexType)` fell through every isinstance check and returned False. Now compares `base_type` strings.
  - **`_types_equal` `char` vs `signed char` collision.** Per C11 6.2.5#15, `char`, `signed char`, and `unsigned char` are three distinct types regardless of platform char-signedness. uc386 represents bare `char` as `BasicType("char", is_signed=None)` and explicit `signed char` as `is_signed=True`. The previous `_types_equal` normalized None → True for ALL types, so plain `char` matched the `signed char` arm in `_Generic` (whichever appeared first). Now `char` keeps the three states distinct; other integer types keep the None ↔ True equivalence.
  - **`_Generic` of a function name used `void *` placeholder type.** uc386's `_identifier_type` returns `PointerType(BasicType("void"))` for function names (a deliberate simplification to dodge pointer-arithmetic scaling). For `_Generic`, that meant `_Generic(helper, int (*)(int): ..., default: ...)` always took the default arm because the controlling type didn't match. Now the `_Generic` dispatch detects function-name controlling expressions and synthesizes the proper `PointerType(FunctionType(ret, params))` from `_func_return_types` / `_func_param_types`.
  - **`ptr + long_long` routed through `_binary_ll`.** `int *p; long long ll = 5; int *q = p + ll;` produced `q` as a 64-bit add of `p`'s 32-bit value and `ll`'s 64-bit value with no scaling — completely wrong. Per C, `ptr + integer` converts the integer to ptrdiff_t (32-bit on i386) and scales by sizeof(*ptr). Fix: in `_binary`, the pointer-arithmetic check (one operand is pointer-like, op is `+`/`-`) now fires BEFORE the long-long short-circuit. `_add_sub` evaluates the LL operand via `_eval_expr_to_eax` which loads only the low 32 bits, then scales — matching the C truncation semantics.
  - **`_eval_expr_to_edx_eax(BinaryOp)` for sub-LL result.** `(long long)(p5 - p)` produced garbage because `_eval_expr_to_edx_eax(BinaryOp)` unconditionally routed to `_binary_ll`, ignoring the BinaryOp's actual result type. ptr-ptr returns int (ptrdiff_t), not LL — `_binary_ll` then read both operands as LL when neither is. Fix: dispatch on `_type_of(BinaryOp)` — if not LL, eval in 32-bit mode and sign/zero-extend EDX per result type's signedness.
  - **`_stripped_callee` over-peeled `*` on pointer-to-pointer-to-function.** `(**(&ops[0]))(5, 5)` for `op_fn ops[3]` (where `op_fn = int (*)(int, int)`) used to call the address `&ops[0]` as code, faulting on first instruction. Per C 6.3.2.1, `*fp` is idempotent ONLY when `fp` is a function pointer (the dereference yields the function which immediately decays back). When `fp` is a pointer-to-pointer-to-function, `*fp` is a real load. The previous `_stripped_callee` blindly peeled all consecutive `*`s, removing the genuine load. Fix: each peel checks the operand's type — peel only when operand is `FunctionType` or `PointerType(FunctionType)`. All callers (`_call_target`, `_call_into_address`, `_call`) now pass `ctx` so the type lookup works.
  - **Anonymous-union member designated init clobbered by end-zero-fill.** `struct{int tag; union{int i; int j;};} x = {.tag=1, .i=99};` had `x.i` clobbered to 0 because `_struct_init`'s end-zero-fill walked unfilled members in declaration order and zero-filled `j`, whose offset (4) overlaps with `i` (offset 4, size 4). Fix: track per-byte filled ranges; skip zero-fill for any member whose bytes are already covered by an initialized peer.
  - **Global anon-union arr over-emits zero bytes.** Same shape but in the global-init path. `_emit_global_struct_init` advanced its emit_cursor by the union's max-member-size after each at-offset run. When the chosen member was the FIRST member of an embedded anon-struct (e.g. `a` of `struct{char a,b;}` at offset 4 within a union), the next iteration would try to emit `b` at offset 5 — but the cursor had already jumped to 8, so `b`'s emit was either skipped or pushed bytes out of place. Fix: detect when the chosen member is part of an anon-struct group whose other members live at higher offsets within the union span; in that case advance by chosen's own size only, so subsequent iterations emit at their correct offsets. Also added a "bytes already covered" guard on uninitialized members to skip them when an initialized peer already wrote those bytes.

  6 new smoke tests + many hand-crafted probes covering each path. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 382/382 (5 new — _types_equal char fix didn't get its own smoke since it's covered by the broader _Generic test). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — `&(scalar T){init}` returned the value instead of the address (real bug)**: `int *p = &(int){100};` set `p = 100` (the value) instead of `p = &temp_holding_100`. `_address_of(Compound)` was implemented as `_eval_expr_to_eax(comp, ctx)`, which for scalar compounds returns the loaded value (not the address). Struct/array compounds return the address (because they go through their respective init helpers + `lea`); scalar compounds were the gap. Fix: dispatch by target type — struct/array stays on the existing path, complex routes through `_complex_value_address(Compound)` (also missing — added), int128 through `_int128_value_address` (already had a Compound branch), long long stores via EDX:EAX, float stores via st(0), and plain int stores via EAX — all explicitly emit `lea eax, &temp` after the store. Verified across `int*` / `long long*` / `double*` / `char*` / `int**` / `unsigned __int128*` / `_Complex double*` / `v4si*` (vector) compound literals.

  No torture/c-testsuite regression (the suites don't exercise this idiom). 1 new smoke test. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 383/383 (1 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — packed structs, anon-union/struct init braces, LU literal mask, _Static_assert in struct, enum array designators (real bugs)**: a sweep of latent bugs surfaced by probing.
  - **`__attribute__((packed))` on structs** was silently ignored. uc_core: parser captures `packed` (mirrors `aligned`) on a new `_pending_packed` flag and threads it through `StructType.is_packed` and `StructDecl.is_packed`. Recognized between `struct` and tag, between tag and `{`, and after closing `}`. uc386: new `_struct_packed` set; `_register_struct` skips natural-alignment offset rounding when packed (every member is byte-aligned, struct's overall alignment is 1); `_alignment_of(StructType)` returns 1 for packed structs.
  - **Anon-union scalar member with brace-init.** `struct V { int kind; union { int i; float f; }; }` initialized with `{3, {.i = 100}}`: previously the inner brace landed on member `i` as an InitializerList (which is a runtime expression, not a value), and the dispatch fell through to `_eval_expr_to_eax`, raising "InitializerList not implemented yet". Both `_struct_init` (locals) and `_emit_global_struct_init` (globals) now unwrap a single-value InitializerList for a scalar promoted-anon member. The unwrapped designator may target a different promoted member of the same union (resolved via `member_index`).
  - **Anon-struct multi-value brace-init.** `struct A { int p; struct { int x, y; }; int s; } a = {1, {2, 3}, 4}`: the inner `{2, 3}` should fill x and y but previously the elision step left it paired with `x` as a 2-value InitializerList, which the scalar dispatch couldn't process. Fix: pre-pass over `elided_values` that detects an InitializerList paired with a promoted-anon-group scalar member and expands it into per-member designated entries using the group span from `_struct_member_groups`. Mirror in `_emit_global_struct_init` for globals.
  - **Cursor advance past anon-promoted group.** After `{1, {.i = 42}, 99}` for `struct B { int n; union {int i; float f;}; int extra; }`, the trailing `99` clobbered `f` instead of `extra` because the cursor advanced from `i` to `f` (the next anon-union alt). Fix: in both local and global designator branches, when a designator targets a member in a multi-member anon-group, advance the cursor past the entire group so the next positional value lands on the next outer subobject.
  - **`0xf2345678LU` constant-folded as long long instead of unsigned long.** uc_core's `_literal_mask` checked `is_long` first (without considering `is_unsigned`); for any value > LONG_MAX, it returned `long_long_mask`, so `0xf2345678LU << 4` produced a 64-bit value with high half 0xF instead of the unsigned-long-truncated 0x2345678F. The runtime computation correctly truncated to 32 bits, so const ≠ runtime in tests like `ROL(ul, shift)` (closes torture 20020508-1, which had regressed). Fix: separate `is_long and is_unsigned` branch (LU/UL → unsigned long, then unsigned long long) and refined the `is_long`-only branch to use the C99 6.4.4.1 walk for hex-with-L (long → unsigned long → long long → unsigned long long) vs decimal-with-L (long → long long).
  - **`_Static_assert` as a struct/union member** (per C11 6.7.2.1) failed with "Expected type specifier". uc_core's struct member parser only consumed type-specifiers; now dispatches `_Static_assert` first, parses the expression and optional message, and silently skips (the assertion isn't evaluated yet — that's a separate gap, not a correctness regression).
  - **Array designator must be IntLiteral.** `enum E { A=1, B=3, C=5 }; int arr[10] = {[A] = 100};` failed with "only single-level integer designators supported in array init" because the dispatch checked `isinstance(designator, IntLiteral)` instead of accepting any constant-integer expression. Fix: when not an IntLiteral, fall back to `_const_eval`. Same fix in `_array_init` (locals) and `_emit_global_array_init` (globals).

  4 new smoke tests targeting the canonical patterns. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 389/389 (6 new). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — typeof aliases, `,##__VA_ARGS__`, DOS-ident as variable, deep anon-struct brace init, scalar `{expr}` unwrap, range designator unsized array (real bugs)**: another sweep of latent bugs surfaced by probing well past the reference suites.
  - **`__typeof__` / `__typeof` aliases.** Recognized in uc_core's `tokens.py` keyword table as TYPEOF aliases. Used heavily in glibc-style header macros (e.g. `MAX(a,b)` expansion). Without this, `__typeof__(x)` produced "Expected SEMICOLON" at the parser. Also fixed `_resolve_typeof_in_body` so that nested typeof-of-stmt-expr-of-typeof chains resolve: included TypeofType-typed VarDecls in `flat_types`; added a StmtExpr branch that returns the trailing expression's type; added a while-loop to chase TypeofType chains in the Identifier branch.
  - **GCC `, ##__VA_ARGS__` comma-swallow.** `#define DBG(fmt, ...) printf(fmt, ##__VA_ARGS__)` invoked as `DBG("hello\n")` (no variadic args) used to leave a trailing `,` in the expansion: `printf("hello\n",)`. Per gcc, a `, ##__VA_ARGS__` (or any `, ##param`) drops the comma when the param expands to empty. Implemented via a regex pre-pass in `_handle_token_pasting` that runs before the regular paste loop.
  - **`int huge = 5;` failed parsing.** uc_core's `_skip_dos_specifiers` swallowed `huge` (in `_DOS_IGNORED_IDENTS`) before the parser saw it as a declarator name — the user's `int huge = 5;` parsed as `int = 5;` and crashed at `=`. Same applied to `near` / `far`. Fix: introduced `_DOS_AMBIGUOUS_IDENTS = {'near', 'far', 'huge'}` (the short, lowercase, un-prefixed names that doubly serve as plausible C identifiers) and a lookahead — only treat them as a specifier if the next token continues a declarator-prefix context (TYPE_SPECIFIERS / STORAGE_CLASSES / FUNCTION_SPECIFIERS / `*` / IDENTIFIER / cv-qualifier). Prefixed forms (`__cdecl`, `__interrupt`, `__extension__`) keep always-skip behavior since they're never used as variable names.
  - **Deep nested anon-struct brace init.** `struct { union { struct { union { struct {xx,yy}; ll }; extra }; buf[20]; }; trailing; }` initialized as `{{{{1, 2}, 99}}, 100}` failed at "InitializerList not implemented yet" because the prior single-level peel-and-spread couldn't track the multi-level anon nesting. Replaced the local-and-global peel logic with a unified `_expand_anon_group_braces` DFS helper (~140 lines) that walks a nested InitializerList inside-out, tracks filled byte ranges across recursive emits, and skips past anon-union members whose bytes are already covered by an init'd peer. Outputs a flat list of DesignatedInit entries that the existing struct-init / global-struct-init dispatch handles uniformly. Mirrors apply to globals via `_emit_global_struct_init`.
  - **Scalar `int x = {42};` and `int *p = {0};`.** C99 6.7.8#11 — braces around a scalar initializer are equivalent to no braces. `_var_init_inner` now unwraps a single-value non-designated InitializerList for non-aggregate scalar targets (BasicType / PointerType / ComplexType — but NOT ArrayType / StructType, which have their own brace-init paths). Same unwrap in `_emit_global_init` for global pointer init (was BasicType-only before).
  - **Per-element scalar `{expr}` unwrap in arrays and structs.** `int arr[3] = {{1}, {2}, {3}};` is per-element-brace-wrapped scalar init — needs unwrapping per element. `_array_init` now unwraps each scalar-targeted element value; `_struct_init` complex member branch does the same. Excludes StructType / ArrayType / Complex element types (those have their own brace-handling paths).
  - **Single-value `_Complex T` brace init preserves imag.** `_Complex double g = {1.0 + 2.0i};` was producing `(1.0, 0.0)` instead of `(1.0, 2.0)` because `_const_eval_complex(InitializerList([expr]))` was discarding the imag part: it returned `(r, 0.0)` after evaluating just the real part of `expr`. Fix: recurse into `expr` so a single-value brace `{1.0 + 2.0i}` flows through the BinaryOp `+` path and preserves imag.
  - **`(int)(float_const)` in const-eval.** `int g = (int)(1.5 + 2.5);` was raising "FloatLiteral not implemented yet" because `_const_eval`'s Cast branch only handled int operands. Fix: try int fold first; if it raises, fall back to `_const_eval_float` and truncate toward zero (C semantics for float→int cast). Stays consistent with the runtime fistp-with-truncation-control-word path.
  - **Unsized array length with designators.** `int *p = (int[]){[0] = 1, [3] = 4};` failed at "index 3 out of range, size 2". `_resolved_var_type` and `_emit_global_array_init` were using `len(values)` as the unsized-array length, but with designators the length is `max(designated_index) + 1`. New `_infer_array_length_from_init` helper walks values handling DesignatedInit, RangeDesignator (`[L ... U] = expr`), and positional values with a cursor. Mirror in `_resolved_var_type` for unsized-local-array length.
  - **Global struct init partial-overlap skip.** `_emit_global_struct_init` could try to emit zero-fill at an offset earlier than `emit_cursor`, since NASM can't seek backward. New "partial overlap" branch: when an unfilled member's range extends past `emit_cursor`, only emit the portion past the cursor (the prior portion is implicitly already in place from a different filled peer). Without this, a unfilled anon-union alt at offset 4 (size 4) following a filled peer at offset 4-8 would try to `times` 4 bytes at a position that's already past 8.

  12 new smoke tests targeting each path. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 403/403 (12 new — the sweep refactor consolidated some prior coverage). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — bool-from-float, complex/vector stmt-expr, label-followed-by-decl, dos_emu printf %c width and %*c sign, complex/int128/vector/struct chained-assign, complex compound chain (real bugs)**: a sweep of latent bugs from probing past the reference suites.
  - **`_Bool b = 0.5;` produced `b = 0`.** `_var_init_inner`'s default scalar path uses `_eval_expr_to_eax` which truncates 0.5 to int 0 via `fistp`, then `_store_from_eax`'s bool normalization sees 0 and stores 0. Per C 6.3.1.2, the conversion is "compares equal to 0", not "truncates to int and tests for non-zero". Fix: route bool-typed local var inits through `_eval_to_bool_eax` instead. Same fix in `_assign` for bool-typed lvalues (any lvalue shape — Identifier / `*p` / `arr[i]` / `s.m`) so `b = 0.5;` and `arr[i] = 0.5;` and `*p = 0.5;` all produce the right 0/1 value via `_eval_to_bool_eax`.
  - **`_Complex` from `({ ...; complex_expr; })` raised "can't take address of complex StmtExpr".** `_complex_value_address` had no StmtExpr branch. Added one — runs head items in scope, then delegates to the trailing expression's complex-address path. Same shape for `_vector_value_address(StmtExpr)` (was raising "vector value: unsupported expression StmtExpr").
  - **C23 6.8.2: label may precede a declaration.** `target: int x = 42;` was rejected with "Unexpected token: INT". uc_core's `_parse_statement`'s LabelStmt branch only called `_parse_statement` for the body. Now dispatches via `_is_declaration_start()` to `_parse_declaration` when applicable. The `LabelStmt(label, stmt=VarDecl)` AST shape is already handled in codegen (since `_item` dispatches both stmts and decls).
  - **dos_emu printf `%c` ignored width.** `printf("[%5c]", 'X')` printed `[X]` instead of `[    X]`. The `%c` branch of `_printf_format` had no width / left-align handling — only `%s` did. Added the same pad logic.
  - **dos_emu printf `%*c` with negative width crashed the emu.** `printf("[%*c]", -5, 'X')` produced "Invalid memory write (UC_ERR_WRITE_UNMAPPED)". `read32_le` returns unsigned, so `-5` came back as `0xFFFFFFFB = 4294967291`. The `if (width < 0)` branch (which handles negative-width-as-left-align per C99 7.21.6.1#5) never fired because the value was unsigned. Same bug in `precision = read32_le(ap_box)` for `%.*` precision. Fix: convert from unsigned to signed (subtract 0x100000000 if high bit set) before the `< 0` test.
  - **Chained struct/complex/int128/vector assignment in expression context.** `a = b = c = X` for these types raised "can't take address of BinaryOp" (or similar) because the inner `b = c = X` is a BinaryOp("=") that's not a regular lvalue. Each address-getter (`_complex_value_address`, `_vector_value_address`, `_binary_int128`) needed a `BinaryOp("=")` case that performs the side-effect (mutating the inner lvalue) and yields the new value's address.
    - `_struct_address` already had the case (line 6322).
    - `_complex_value_address`: gained a comma-op branch that side-effect-evaluates the lhs (type-aware, so a complex lhs uses `_complex_value_address` instead of `_eval_expr_to_eax` which can't load 16 bytes).
    - `_vector_value_address`: gained `=` and compound-op branches that route through `_vector_copy_assign` / `_compound_assign_vector_lvalue` and then re-derive the lhs address.
    - `_binary_int128`: gained `=` and compound-op branches that route through `_int128_copy_assign` and then copy the lhs's value into dest.
  - **Complex compound assignment in expression context (`a += b += rhs`).** Two related bugs:
    - `_eval_complex_into_top` had no compound-op branch — fell through to `_scalar_to_complex_into_top` which evaluated the complex RHS as a float (giving real-only with garbage). Added a compound-op handler that executes the side-effect via `_compound_assign_complex_lvalue` and copies the lvalue's new value to TOS dest.
    - `_compound_assign_complex_lvalue` for Identifier desugared by re-using the compound op (`a += b` → `BinaryOp("+=", a, b)`) — so the inner BinaryOp was identical to the outer, causing recursion when the new dispatch above was added. Fix: strip `=` via `_COMPOUND_OPS` lookup to get the base op (`+=` → `+`). Same fix in the non-Identifier path.
  - **`_Complex` comma operator with complex result.** `c = (a = X, b)` for complex c, b raised "can't load size-16 value into eax" because `_eval_complex_into_top` had no comma branch and fell to `_scalar_to_complex_into_top` which tried to eval the comma as a float. Same shape fix as the chained-assign — type-aware lhs side-effect eval, then yield rhs's complex value into the dest.
  - **Struct comma operator** (`x = (side_effect, struct_value)`). `_struct_address` had no comma branch. Added one — eval lhs for side effects, return rhs's struct address.

  9 new smoke tests + many hand-crafted probes. **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite (both 100%)**. Smoke 411/411 (8 new — bool-init, bool-assign, %c width, %*c star, complex stmt-expr, vector stmt-expr, label-decl, complex compound chain). Pipeline: 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — `va_arg` not recognized as having side effects (real bug)**: uc_core's `_expr_has_side_effects` predicate gates the optimizer's `x * 2 → x + x` strength reduction (and several other rewrites that duplicate operands). It returned `True` for `Call`, `StmtExpr`, `++`/`--`, and any assignment, but had no case for `VaArgExpr`. Result: `va_arg(ap, int) * 2` got rewritten to `va_arg(ap, int) + va_arg(ap, int)`, advancing the va_list pointer twice and skipping a value. Fix: added `if isinstance(expr, ast.VaArgExpr): return True` in uc_core's optimizer. The reference suites didn't catch this because the torture/c-testsuite va_arg tests don't multiply va_arg results by powers of 2 in a single expression. Smoke test runs the optimizer explicitly (since `_compile` skips it) and counts `add dword [ebp - 4], 4` (advance-ap-by-sizeof(int)) inside the test function — buggy form has 2 occurrences, fixed form has 1.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (412 total).
- **2026-04-28 — `Member`/`Compound` not recognized as side-effect-bearing (real bugs)**: walking the same `_expr_has_side_effects` predicate revealed two more gaps. Both fired the same `x * 2 → x + x` strength-reduction bug as `va_arg`.
  - **Member access** (`s.m`, `p->m`). The access itself isn't a side effect, but the OBJECT expression may be. The predicate had no `Member` case, so `make().x * 2` got rewritten to `make().x + make().x`, calling `make()` twice. Same bug for `getp()->x * 2` and `arr[side()].x * 2`. Fix: recurse into `expr.obj`. Also benefits the dead-store eliminator at line 1451 (`b = make().x; b = 42;` would have dropped the first store and skipped the call).
  - **Compound literal** (`(T){init}`). The initializers run when the literal is materialized. Predicate had no `Compound` case, so `(struct S){f()}.x * 2` called `f()` twice. Fix: recurse into `expr.init` (an `InitializerList`). Also added an `InitializerList` case that walks each value (and `DesignatedInit.value`s) so the recursion bottoms out cleanly.
  - The reference suites didn't catch these because they don't do `x * 2` strength reduction on side-effect-bearing Member or Compound expressions.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +2 smoke tests (414 total).
- **2026-04-28 — `_Bool` from float in array / struct / global init (real bug)**: per C 6.3.1.2 a `_Bool` conversion compares against 0 (any non-zero → 1, zero → 0). Earlier I'd fixed scalar locals (`_Bool b = 0.5;` via `_eval_to_bool_eax`) but missed three sibling sites:
  - **`_Bool arr[N] = {..., 0.5, ...}`** in `_array_init` fell through the per-element fallback `_eval_expr_to_eax` + `_store_from_eax`. For a float source, `_eval_expr_to_eax` truncates via `fistp` (so `0.5 → 0`), which is the WRONG conversion for `_Bool`. Fix: recognize bool element type and route through `_eval_to_bool_eax`.
  - **`struct S { _Bool b; ... } s = {0.5, ...}`** in `_struct_init` had the same fallthrough. Fix: same dispatch.
  - **`_Bool g = 0.5;` (and global arrays / struct members) in `_emit_global_init`** raised "initializer must be a constant expression" because `_const_eval` (integer-only) rejected `FloatLiteral`. Fix: for bool target, try `_const_eval` first, fall back to `_const_eval_float` on failure, then normalize to 0/1. Same fallback in the bool-array global directive path.
  - Probed by `_Bool arr[5] = {0, 1, 5, -1, 0.1};` reading `arr[4] != 1` and aborting. Reference suites use bool with int literals only; no test exercises bool-from-float.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +3 smoke tests (417 total).
- **2026-04-28 — `_Bool` compound assign on non-Identifier lvalue with wide rhs (real bug)**: `*p += 0.7` / `arr[i] += 0.7` / `s.m += 0.7` / `s.bf += 0.7` for `_Bool` lvalues with float / long long / int128 / complex rhs all produced 0 instead of 1. Per C, `b += 0.7` is `b = (bool)((double)b + 0.7)` — arithmetic in the wider type, then cast to bool. The bug: `_compound_assign` for non-Identifier lvalues did `_eval_expr_to_eax(rhs)` which truncates 0.7 to int 0, then 0 + 0 = 0, then stored 0 (with bool normalization at store-time, which doesn't help — the value was already 0). Same bug for the bit-field compound-assign path.
  - **Identifier path was already correct** because it desugars to `b = b + rhs` and routes through `_assign`, which has a bool-target branch (line 15128) that uses `_eval_to_bool_eax` on the rhs — which knows about float/LL/int128/complex.
  - **Fix for non-Identifier lvalues** (`*p`, `arr[i]`, `s.m`): new `_compound_assign_bool_lvalue` snapshot pattern. Compute &lvalue once into a hidden 4-byte addr slot, then synthesize `*addr = (*addr) OP rhs` and route through `_assign` (whose bool target path handles float-rhs correctly). The synthesized `*addr` lvalue is side-effect-free to re-read since `addr` is a regular local.
  - **Fix for bool bit-fields** (`s.bf op= rhs`): new `_compound_assign_bool_bitfield`. Compute &storage_unit, save in addr slot. Read field value (0 or 1) into a hidden 1-byte bool snap slot. Synthesize `snap = snap OP rhs` and route through `_assign` (bool Identifier path → `_eval_to_bool_eax`). Read snap back, RMW the storage unit.
  - Reference suites don't trigger this — they don't compound-assign float / LL to bool lvalues. Probed with `*p += 0.7`, `arr[i] += 0.5`, `s.m += 0.5`, `s.b -= 1.0`, `*get_p() += 0.7` (side-effect lvalue fires once), `arr[i++] += 0.5` (single-fire i++).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +2 smoke tests (419 total).
- **2026-04-28 — `sizeof(arr + 1)` returned full array size (real bug, was a known limitation)**: from CLAUDE.md slice 12 — `sizeof(arr + 0)` returned the full array size instead of pointer size because `_type_of` didn't decay arrays in arithmetic results. Per C, an array in arithmetic context (`arr + N`, `arr - N`) decays to a pointer; the result of the `+` is `int *`, not `int [N]`. Fix: in `_type_of(BinaryOp("+"|"-"))`'s pointer-propagation branch, when the propagated operand is `ArrayType`, return `PointerType(base_type=arr.base_type)` instead. Smoke test verifies `sizeof(arr + 1)` is 4. The arr-arithmetic scaling and ptr-ptr subtraction paths are unaffected because they only need the pointee size, which is preserved.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (420 total).
- **2026-04-28 — Vector in boolean context always truthy (real bug)**: `if (v)` / `v ? a : b` / `!v` for a GCC-extension `vector_size`-typed value always took the truthy branch. `_eval_to_bool_eax` had no case for vector — fell through to `_eval_expr_to_eax(vector_expr)` which returns the vector's address (always non-zero), so even an all-zero vector tested as truthy. Fix: when the operand is `ArrayType` with `is_vector=True`, OR all the dwords of the vector value together and setne. Per GCC extension, vector booleans are "any element non-zero". Smoke test verifies a zero vector in a ternary condition selects the false arm.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (421 total).
- **2026-04-28 — Loop condition optimized with stale copy-prop cache (real bug)**: `int *p = head; while (p) { p = next; }` ran forever (or against an unmutated address) because the optimizer's level-3 copy-propagation rewrote the loop condition's `p` back to `head` (using the pre-loop `_copies = {p: head}` cache). The body's `p = next;` invalidates the copy, but the condition was ALREADY optimized using the stale cache before the body was looked at. uc_core's WhileStmt path cleared caches BEFORE the body but AFTER optimizing the condition. Same shape in ForStmt — init's effects on the cache could leak into condition / update optimization. Fix: clear caches BEFORE optimizing the condition for WhileStmt, and BEFORE the condition / update for ForStmt. The condition / update may run after the body has mutated state, so prior-cache rewrites are unsound. The reference suites didn't catch this because their loops don't use `while (p) p = p->next;` patterns where `p` is a copy of an outer var.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +1 smoke test (422 total).
- **2026-04-28 — Phase A peephole: framework + dead-after-jmp + jmp-to-next**: kicked off the post-codegen optimization pass. New `src/uc386/peephole.py` parses asm into classified Lines (instr / label / directive / data / comment / blank) and runs patterns to fixed point. Two patterns landed: (1) `dead_after_terminator` drops everything between an unconditional `jmp` / `ret` / `iret` / `retf` / `retn` and the next label / directive / data line. (2) `jmp_to_next_label` drops `jmp X` immediately followed by `X:` (skipping intervening blanks/comments). Wired into `CodeGenerator(peephole=True)` (default on), with `--no-peephole` CLI flag and per-pattern hit counts under `-v`. Smoke `_compile()` opts out so existing assertions against the unoptimized emission shape continue to hold. New `tests/test_peephole.py` with 17 tests covering both patterns, near-miss cases (conditional jumps, indirect jumps, distant labels), and codegen integration. Also wrote `PEEPHOLE_PLAN.md` with the full optimization roadmap (phases A–I) modeled on uc80 + upeepz80: peephole, asm DCE, multi-file/whole-program, embedded runtime with selective inclusion, printf auto-detection + puts rewrite, function inlining, interprocedural const-prop, shared storage, and eventual `upeep386` extraction. The two patterns alone shave ~5% off representative small programs (12 lines from a 226-line baseline). Each codegen function-end currently emits `mov eax, 0; jmp .epilogue; xor eax, eax; .epilogue:`; the peephole reduces that to just `mov eax, 0; .epilogue:`.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +17 peephole tests; smoke unchanged (422). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-28 — Phase A peephole: binop_collapse + store_collapse**: collapses the per-binop and per-store stack-machine slack visible in every codegen output. The prior pass dropped only end-of-function dead code; these patterns target the body. New helpers: `_operands_split` (parse `dst, src`), `_references_register` (word-boundary regex), `_is_simple_eax_load` (one-instr `mov eax, src`), `_retarget_eax_to_ecx`, `_next_n_instrs` (collect N instr lines, fail past fence). New patterns:
  - **`binop_collapse`** matches `push eax; mov eax, src; mov ecx, eax; pop eax` and replaces it with a single `mov ecx, src`. Saves 3 instructions per match. Fires on every binop's right-operand load: `cmp`, `add`, `sub`, `imul`, `cdq+idiv`, all comparison ops, all shift ops.
  - **`store_collapse`** matches `push eax; mov eax, src; pop ecx; mov [ecx], eax` and replaces it with `mov ecx, eax; mov eax, src; mov [ecx], eax`. Saves 1 instruction (push+pop pair → mov ecx, eax). Net savings smaller than binop because the address-into-ECX retarget on the previous instruction is deferred.
  - **Both patterns reject ESP-relative sources.** A `push eax` decreases ESP by 4; any `mov eax, [esp + N]` in the middle reads from a location whose offset depends on the push. After collapse, ESP wouldn't be shifted and the `[esp + N]` reads a different byte. Caught by c-testsuite 00217 (`*(unsigned*)(data + r) += a - b;` whose codegen reads `[esp + 4]` to reach over an inner push) and 22 torture tests with similar nested-push patterns. The fix: both `_matches_binop_collapse` and `_matches_store_collapse` reject when `src` references ESP. The first run of the suites caught all of these.
  - **store_collapse rejects ECX-reading sources** for the same reason — the saved address would alias the source's load.

  On a representative small program (`probe_size.c`: 3 functions plus main with printf calls): 226 → 190 lines = 16% reduction. binop_collapse fires 8 times (every comparison and every loop-step), store_collapse fires 4 times (one per assignment to `*p` / `arr[i]`).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +9 peephole tests (33 total); smoke unchanged (422). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: leave_collapse**: replaces every function epilogue's `mov esp, ebp; pop ebp` with the equivalent single-byte `leave` instruction. NASM emits `leave` as 0xC9 (1 byte) vs the 0x89 0xEC 0x5D triple (3 bytes). Saves 1 instruction + 2 bytes per function epilogue. Fires once per function in our codegen — every function uses the standard `push ebp; mov ebp, esp; ...; mov esp, ebp; pop ebp; ret` frame. The pattern matches `mov esp, ebp` followed by `pop ebp` (with blanks/comments tolerated between). Doesn't fire when the pattern is incomplete (e.g., a fragment with `mov esp, ebp; ret`). 4 hits on probe_size.c (one per function); proportional to function count on real programs.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +3 peephole tests (36 total); smoke unchanged (422). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: imm_store_collapse**: collapses `mov eax, IMM; mov [addr], eax; mov eax, X` to `mov dword [addr], IMM; mov eax, X`. The third instruction's EAX overwrite is the witness that EAX was dead after the store — without that witness, EAX might be carrying the assignment expression's value for use in a comparison/return/etc. NASM's `mov dword [addr], IMM` form encodes directly without going through EAX. Matches when src is a constant expression (no `[` for memory deref, not a bare register). 5 tests covering positive/negative cases (immediate, label, memory-source rejection, no-witness rejection, register-source rejection). Saves 1 instruction per match. 1 hit on probe_size.c (the `int s = 0;` for-init).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +5 peephole tests (41 total); smoke unchanged (422). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: setcc_jcc_collapse**: collapses every `if (...)` / `while (...)` / `for (cond; ...)` / `?:` in the codebase. The boolean-materialize-then-branch chain `setCC al; movzx eax, al; test eax, eax; jz/jnz LBL` becomes a single `j<cc> LBL` with the right inversion (jz after setCC inverts the condition; jnz keeps it). 18-entry CC inverse table covers e/ne, l/le/g/ge, b/be/a/ae, s/ns, o/no, p/np plus aliases (z/nz, c/nc, pe/po). 6 hits on probe_size.c — every comparison fires (`if`, `for`-cond, etc.). Saves 3 instructions per match. **probe_size.c down from 226 to 167 lines = 26.1% total reduction across all 7 patterns.**

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +5 peephole tests (46 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase D slice 1: selective libc inclusion**: huge binary-size win. Every uc386-compiled binary previously embedded the full 3547-line monolithic libc (~6 KB of code) regardless of what the user actually called. New `src/uc386/libc_split.py` parses libc into per-function units (187 functions + 9 data labels), tracks each function's deps via regex scan over its body, and computes the transitive closure from the user's actual call sites. Modified `dos_emu.bundle_user_asm()` to embed only the reached functions (default on; `selective_libc=False` falls back to monolithic for safety).
  - **Hello-world: 5891 → 123 bytes** (47x reduction)
  - **probe_size.c (printf, fact, sum, classify): 6248 → 480 bytes** (13x reduction)
  - Avg 76% reduction across c-testsuite test binaries; biggest wins on programs that don't touch float/string libc.
  - Two key bug fixes during integration:
    1. The label regex `_[A-Za-z][A-Za-z0-9_]*` rejected `___builtin_*` names (second char is `_`, not `[A-Za-z]`). Fixed to `_[_A-Za-z][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. Found via initial torture run with 310 regressions on tests using `___builtin_printf` / `___builtin_memcpy` etc.
    2. Initial seed strategy used `extern _name` declarations as roots — but `<math.h>` declares 162 math functions, all of which would then be pulled in. Switched to scanning for any `_*` reference in non-comment lines (call targets, address loads, push immediates, data refs). Extern declarations alone are now ignored.
  - Data section (`.data` + `.bss`) is always emitted in full — small (16 lines), and tracking data deps would add complexity for no measurable win.
  - +19 libc_split tests covering parsing, dep extraction, transitive closure (with cycles), emit, and integration with the real libc file.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +19 libc_split tests (461 total smoke + peephole + libc_split). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — `_start` skips FPU/BSS init when not needed**: the entry stub used to unconditionally emit FPU control-word setup (4 lines) and BSS zero-init (6 lines) before calling main. New `_needs_fpu_init` and `_needs_bss_init` predicates skip each block when the program doesn't need it.
  - **`_needs_bss_init`**: checks for at least one non-noinit uninitialized global. Hello-world has none → BSS init dropped.
  - **`_needs_fpu_init`**: checks for any user-visible (non-builtin) function or global with float/double/long-double/complex type. Filters out `__builtin_isinff` and the 16 other auto-registered builtin sigs that would otherwise trip the check on every program. `_type_uses_float` walks types recursively (struct members, array elements, pointee) with cycle protection for self-referential structs (`struct list { list *next; ... };`).
  - **Hello-world: 123 → 91 bytes** (32 bytes saved). With selective libc + this, hello-world's `_start` is 3 instructions: `call _main; mov ah, 4Ch; int 21h`.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: push_immediate**: collapses every cdecl arg-push site. The codegen emits `mov eax, X; push eax` for each arg in a `f(arg1, arg2, ...)` call; that's 6 bytes (5 for `mov eax, imm32` + 1 for `push eax`) where `push imm32` alone would be 5 bytes (or 2 bytes for `push imm8`). Rewrites to `push X` when the next instruction overwrites EAX (mov eax, * / xor eax, eax / call * / lea eax, * / pop eax) — the witness that EAX was just being staged for the push. Skipped when src is a memory deref (NASM has no equivalent single-instruction mem-imm push form).
  - 9 hits on probe_size.c (every arg push).
  - probe_size.c: 226 → **148 lines** (34.5% total reduction across all 8 peephole patterns).
  - Hello-world: 95 → 91 bytes (4 bytes via push_immediate's 1-byte saving + dead_after_terminator's 3-byte xor elimination).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. +5 peephole tests (51 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Skip EBP frame for trivial leaf functions**: when a function has no params, no locals, no VLAs, no nested-fn trampoline, no instrumentation, and doesn't return a struct/complex/vector/int128 (which use the retptr ABI requiring [ebp + 8] access), skip the entire `push ebp; mov ebp, esp; ... mov esp, ebp; pop ebp` frame. Saves 4 bytes per qualifying function. 4 torture failures during integration (`pr43784`, `20020810-1`, `20131127-1`, `pr60017`) — all struct-returning functions with no source-level params; the codegen emits a hidden `__retptr__` param that lives at [ebp + 8] which my predicate hadn't excluded. Fix: also gate on the retptr-using return types. Hello-world: 91 → 87 bytes (`_main` no longer has a frame; just `push _str; call _printf; add esp, 4; mov eax, 0; ret`).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture, 220/220 c-testsuite still 100%**. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: imm_binop_collapse + mov_zero_to_xor + store_load_collapse**: three more patterns that compound. Together they fold the most common stack-machine slack the codegen produces.
  - **imm_binop_collapse**: `mov ecx, <src>; OP eax, ecx` → `OP eax, <src>` for OP ∈ {add, sub, and, or, xor, cmp, test, imul, adc, sbb}. Source is anything except an ECX self-reference (CX/CL/CH all blocked too) — immediate, label, memory operand (`[ebp - N]`, `[_glob]`), or register. Witness for ECX-dead: next instr overwrites ECX (full mov/pop/xor/lea/call) or doesn't reference any ECX alias. Saves 3-6 bytes per match (the prior `mov ecx, src` instruction). Common at every constant comparison (`if (x > 5)` → `cmp eax, 5` instead of `mov ecx, 5; cmp eax, ecx`) and every memory-source binop (`a + b[i]` → `add eax, [b+i]` instead of `mov ecx, [b+i]; add eax, ecx`).
  - **mov_zero_to_xor**: `mov reg, 0` → `xor reg, reg` for any 32-bit gp reg. Saves 3 bytes per match (5-byte mov-imm32 → 2-byte xor reg, reg). Conservative flag analysis: scan forward up to 20 instructions; safe if a flag-CLOBBERING op or `ret`/`call` appears before any flag-READING op (jcc, setcc, cmovcc, adc, sbb, rcl, rcr, loope/loopne, into, pushf, lahf). Crosses labels and unconditional jumps under the codegen invariant that flag state is never assumed to carry across labels (every entry to a labeled block re-establishes flags via cmp/test before any conditional branch).
  - **store_load_collapse**: `mov [<addr>], <reg>; mov <reg>, [<addr>]` → just the store. The register still holds its stored value, so the load is redundant. Address comparison is textual (after whitespace normalization) — works for both [ebp - N] locals and [_glob] globals. Common after `int x = call(); if (x ...)` patterns where the codegen stores then immediately reloads.

  Cumulative result on the `_strncmp_test` probe: each `cmp eax, ecx` paired with `mov ecx, [ebp + N]` collapsed to `cmp eax, [ebp + N]`; same for the seven `add eax, ecx; mov ecx, [ebp - 4]` pairs in pointer arithmetic; `xor eax, eax` replaces `mov eax, 0` four times; the redundant `mov eax, [ebp - 4]` after the call's store is dropped.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +18 peephole tests (510 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: right_operand_retarget**: the multi-instruction binop RHS chain now retargets directly to ECX, dropping the entire `push eax / chain / mov ecx, eax / pop eax` save/restore scaffold. Saves 4 bytes per binop with non-trivial RHS (push + mov + pop = 4 bytes total).
  - Match (looking back from `mov ecx, eax; pop eax`): `push eax` followed by N >= 1 chain instructions, all of which write EAX as their dest. The chain's first instruction must be a "fresh write" (mov / lea / pop / xor reg+reg / call) — not a RMW that reads EAX's prior value (the LHS).
  - Each chain instruction's source operand must not reference ECX/CX/CL/CH (else retargeting would self-reference) or `[esp + N]` (else dropping the surrounding push/pop changes which byte is read).
  - cmp/test/xchg/cdq are excluded (read EAX without writing, or have unusual semantics under retarget).
  - The retarget pass replaces `eax`/`ax`/`al`/`ah` in operands with `ecx`/`cx`/`cl`/`ch` respectively, so any sub-byte aliasing is handled correctly.
  - Drops the `mov ecx, eax` step, the leading `push eax`, AND the trailing `pop eax`. EAX is preserved naturally because the retargeted chain only writes ECX.
  - Most common shape lifted: pointer-arithmetic + byte deref (`a[i]`) where each operand expands to `mov; add; movsx`. Without retarget that's `push eax; mov; add; movsx; mov ecx, eax; pop eax` (6 instr); with retarget: `mov; add; movsx` to ecx (3 instr).
  - probe_misc: 2483 → 2353 bytes ASM (-130 bytes); 188 → 180 bytes COM (-8 bytes after libc dedup).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests (517 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%). Total benchmark size reduction climbs to 27.1%.
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: cmp_zero_to_test + dead_mov_to_eax**: two more refinements.
  - **cmp_zero_to_test**: `cmp <reg>, 0` → `test <reg>, <reg>`. Saves 1 byte per match (3-byte cmp-imm8-sign-ext → 2-byte test). Identical flag effects for ZF/SF/OF/CF/PF — JCCs after either form see the same flag state.
  - **dead_mov_to_eax**: drop `mov eax, <src>` (or `lea/movsx/movzx`) when forward CFG-aware scan finds a pure overwrite of EAX before any read. Restricted to EAX because uc386's nested-fn trampoline convention sets ECX as an implicit input to certain calls — dropping a `mov ecx, X` before such a call would break the static-link mechanism.
    - **CFG-aware scan**: at unconditional `jmp X`, follows the target label (does NOT continue text fallthrough — that's unreachable from this CFG path). At conditional jumps, conservatively bails (would need to verify both successors).
