  - **Restricted to dst != ECX** since dropping the only definition of ECX would make the destination undefined (any subsequent ECX read would also see undefined). The codegen never emits `mov ecx, IMM; shl ecx, cl` directly — that would be `ecx = IMM << ecx` which is incoherent.
  - **Restricted to IMM in [0, 31]** for safety. x86 hardware masks shift count to 31 anyway, but NASM accepts the imm form for these values without warnings.
  - **Sample fire rate**: 13 of 200 random torture tests with 99 total fires (~7-8 fires per matching test). High-impact pass.
  - **Concrete example**: `(x << 1) + (x << 3) + (x >> 2) + (x >> 4)` lowers to `mov eax, [x]; shl eax, 1; mov ecx, [x]; shl ecx, 3; add eax, ecx; mov ecx, [x]; sar ecx, 2; add eax, ecx; mov ecx, [x]; sar ecx, 4; add eax, ecx` — was 4 fewer instructions when each `mov ecx, N` was paired with `shl/sar eax, cl`.
  - **Synergy with `right_operand_retarget`**: after my pass collapses to `shl eax, N`, the chain becomes a 2-instruction EAX-writing chain (`mov eax, [x]; shl eax, N`). retarget then rewrites the chain to write ECX directly, dropping the surrounding push/pop save-frame.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +11 peephole tests (875 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: div_mem_form**: collapse `mov reg, [m]; <ext>; div/idiv reg` into `<ext>; div/idiv [m]`. The codegen lowers division by loading the divisor into a scratch register first; x86's div/idiv accept a memory-form divisor directly. Saves 2 bytes per match (drops the 3-byte `mov reg, [m]`; gains 1 byte for the mem-form div/idiv).
  - **Both signed and unsigned**: `mov reg, [m]; cdq; idiv reg` → `cdq; idiv [m]`; `mov reg, [m]; xor edx, edx; div reg` → `xor edx, edx; div [m]`.
  - **Restricted to scratch regs** ebx/ecx/esi/edi for the source (not eax/edx — those hold the dividend).
  - **Restricted to memory operands not referencing eax/edx** (those get clobbered before the div reads).
  - **Sample fire rate**: 6 of 200 random torture tests (28 fires total). About 4-5 fires per matching test — solid impact for arithmetic-heavy programs.
  - **Concrete example**: `int divtest(int a, int b) { return a / b; }` lowers to `mov eax, [ebp+8]; mov ecx, [ebp+12]; cdq; idiv ecx`. After my pass: `mov eax, [ebp+8]; cdq; idiv dword [ebp+12]`. One instruction shorter, 2 bytes saved per division.
  - **Pass order**: runs after rmw_collapse and before shift_const_imm. Independent of both — div uses a fixed register pair (edx:eax for dividend, single reg for divisor), distinct from rmw and shift patterns.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +10 peephole tests (885 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: mov_test_setcc_movzx_collapse**: collapse the 4-instruction boolean-materialize pattern `mov reg, [m]; test reg, reg; setCC al; movzx eax, al` into `cmp dword [m], 0; setCC al; movzx eax, al`. Saves 1 byte per match. Common in `x == 0`, `x != 0`, `x > 0`, `!x`, etc. used in expression context (assigned to var, returned, used in arithmetic).
  - **Why is this safe?** The `mov reg, [m]` loads [m] into reg (full width), then `test reg, reg` sets ZF/SF based on reg. `setCC al` writes AL based on flags; `movzx eax, al` zero-extends AL into EAX. The high bits of reg/EAX after the mov/test/setCC are [m]'s high bytes, but movzx discards them — so the intermediate full-EAX-load is unused. `cmp dword [m], 0` produces equivalent flags (both test for [m] == 0 with SF = high bit of [m], CF=OF=0).
  - **All standard setCC variants supported**: sete/setne/setl/setg/setle/setge/seta/setb/setae/setbe/sets/setns/seto/setno/setp/setnp plus aliases (setz/setnz/setc/setnc/setpe/setpo).
  - **Any GP32 source register** for the original load — typically EAX, but earlier passes (right_operand_retarget) may rewrite to ECX/EBX/etc.
  - **[m] must not reference EAX** since the rewrite uses memory addressing and EAX is the final destination via setCC + movzx.
  - **Sample fire rate**: 5 fires across 200 random torture tests (one per matching test). Modest but real. Combined with `cmp_load_collapse` (which handles `mov reg, [m]; cmp reg, X; jcc` for control flow), this completes coverage of the load-then-test idiom for both branch and value contexts.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +10 peephole tests (895 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: rmw_mem_src_collapse**: collapse compound-assign-with-memory-rhs chains. Pattern `mov reg, [m1]; OP reg, [m2]; mov [m1], reg` → `mov reg, [m2]; OP [m1], reg` for OP ∈ {add, sub, and, or, xor}. Saves 3 bytes per match (drops the original load + store = 6 bytes; gains the same-width load of [m2] and the mem-form OP = 6 bytes; net is 3 bytes shorter overall... wait actually: original = 3 instr × 3 bytes each = 9 bytes; rewrite = 2 instr × 3 bytes each = 6 bytes; saves 3 bytes).
  - **Why this works**: x86 has no mem-mem OP form (`add [m1], [m2]` doesn't exist), but `add [m1], reg` does. By loading [m2] into reg INSTEAD of [m1], we get a 2-instruction in-place RMW.
  - **Differs from `rmw_collapse`**: that pass handles immediate or register source (no memory). `rmw_mem_src_collapse` handles memory source by rearranging which mem becomes the dest.
  - **Common in `s += i;`-style compound assigns** where both operands are memory. After binop_collapse merges `mov ecx, [i]; add eax, ecx` into `add eax, [i]`, my pass turns the surrounding `mov eax, [s]; ...; mov [s], eax` frame into `add [s], eax` directly.
  - **Cascades with `redundant_eax_load`**: in for-loop bodies like `for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) s += i;`, the loop top already loads `i` into EAX (`mov eax, [i]`) for the cmp. My rewrite produces `mov eax, [i]` then `add [s], eax`. The `mov eax, [i]` is then dropped by redundant_eax_load (EAX already holds [i]). Loop body shrinks from 3 instructions (load s, add i, store s) to 1 (`add [s], eax`).
  - **Restricted to `[ebp ± N]` and `[_label]`** for both operands (frame slots and globals — no register-base derefs to avoid aliasing concerns).
  - **Sample fire rate**: 2 of 200 random torture tests. Modest but real, with the cascade benefit being where the bigger savings come from.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +10 peephole tests (905 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: dead_stack_store extended for sizeless register stores**: the existing `dead_stack_store` pass required an explicit size prefix in `mov dword [ebp ± N], V`. But the codegen often emits the register form `mov [ebp ± N], reg` WITHOUT a size prefix (NASM infers size from the source register). These dead stores weren't being detected. Extended `_stack_store_offset` to also recognize the no-size-prefix form when the source is a 32-bit GP register (sub-registers are conservatively skipped to avoid partial-overwrite confusion).
  - **Concrete impact**: chained statement assigns like `y = x; y += 5; y *= 2;` lower to three back-to-back `mov [ebp - 4], eax` stores. Before this extension, the first two stores survived as dead code. After: all but the final store are dropped. Saves ~3 bytes per dead intermediate store.
  - **Sample fire rate**: 2 of 200 random torture tests with this extension. Modest direct impact, but cleaner code (and removes an obvious "why is this dead store still here" issue when reading codegen output).
  - **Why this matters**: dead_stack_store's job is to catch dead intermediate stores. The codegen sometimes produces them (chained assigns, struct init followed by member overwrite). The pass was working for size-prefixed stores (struct-init `mov dword [m], imm` form) but missing the register-store case. Now both are handled.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +4 peephole tests (909 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: reg_copy_addr_forward + 2 latent-bug fixes**: collapse `mov REGB, REGA; <instr using [REGB...]>` into `<instr using [REGA...]>` when REGB is dead after. Saves 2 bytes per match (drops the 2-byte register copy). Common after `*p = V` / `*p` lowering: codegen emits `lea reg, addr; mov ecx, reg; mov [ecx], V` (or `mov dst, [ecx]`); my pass collapses the `mov ecx, reg; mov [ecx], V` pair.
  - **High fire rate**: 38 of 200 random torture tests fire (71 fires total, ~1.9 per matching test). Most impactful new pass yet.
  - **Adding this surfaced two pre-existing latent bugs in `_reg_dead_after`**, both visible only when analyzing EBP/ESP liveness:
    - **`leave` not recognized as reading EBP/ESP**. The `leave` instruction is `mov esp, ebp; pop ebp` — it READS EBP and writes both EBP and ESP. The existing `_reg_dead_after` walked past `leave` as if it had no implicit register reads, then hit `ret` which returned True (dead) for non-EAX/EDX regs. Fixed by adding a special-case for `leave`: returns False (alive) for EBP/ESP, continues scanning for other regs (which leave doesn't touch).
    - **`_find_label_idx` ignored NASM local-label scoping**. NASM scopes `.local` labels to the most recent non-local label. Two functions can each have their own `.L2_endif:` — they're DIFFERENT labels. The existing `_find_label_idx` returned the FIRST matching label by text, which often pointed to the wrong scope's label. Fixed by adding an optional `from_idx` parameter: when the label starts with `.`, the function finds the scope owner (most recent non-local label before `from_idx`) and searches within that scope only (until the next non-local label). For non-local labels or when no `from_idx` is given, falls back to first-match.
    - These bugs were latent because no other pass tried to analyze EBP liveness through control flow (most passes care about EAX/ECX/EDX, which get clobbered by calls anyway). Without these fixes, my pass turned `mov ebp, esp; cmp [ebp + 16], 0; ...` into `cmp [esp + 16], 0; ...` (dropping `mov ebp, esp`) — wrong because subsequent code in the function still references [ebp + N].
  - **Pattern conditions**: REG copy from REGA to REGB (both GP32, REGA != REGB); next instruction uses REGB in addressing; REGB dead after that instruction; REGA isn't being modified by the next instruction. Substitute REGB with REGA in the addressing.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +9 peephole tests (918 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: lea_sib_load_collapse**: extends `lea_load_collapse` to handle (a) non-adjacent lea + load (intermediate independent instructions allowed) and (b) SIB-form addressing `[REG + IDX*SCALE + DISP]`. Pattern `lea REG, [ebp ± N]; <indep>; mov REG2, [REG + IDX*SCALE]` → `<indep>; mov REG2, [ebp ± N + IDX*SCALE]`. Drops the 3-byte lea.
  - **Common in local array indexing**: `int x[5]; ... s += x[i];` lowers to `lea eax, [ebp - 20]; mov ecx, [i]; mov eax, [eax + ecx*4]; add [s], eax`. After this pass: `mov ecx, [i]; mov eax, [ebp + ecx*4 - 20]; add [s], eax`. Saves 3 bytes per iteration of an array-access loop.
  - **Conditions**: lea source is `[ebp ± N]`; intermediate lines (up to 8 instructions) don't touch the lea target register; the load uses the lea target as base; the lea target is dead after the load (or is overwritten BY the load, which is the common case).
  - **Folds disp into addressing**: combined offset `lea_disp + load_disp` is computed at peephole time. The new addressing uses NASM's flexible form `[ebp + ecx*4 - 20]` which assembles to a single sib-with-disp8 or disp32 form.
  - **Pass order**: runs AFTER `lea_load_collapse` so that pass can handle the simple adjacent + non-SIB case first. My pass picks up the residual: non-adjacent (intermediate instructions present) and SIB-form addressing.
  - **Sample fire rate**: 8 of 200 random torture tests (9 fires total). Modest but real, especially in array-indexing-heavy code.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +7 peephole tests (925 total). Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: value_forward_to_reg handles memory sources**: extends `value_forward_to_reg` to allow memory sources in addition to immediates / labels / register sources. Pattern `mov reg1, [m]; mov reg2, reg1` collapses to `mov reg2, [m]` when reg1 is dead after. The new memory load is the same encoded width as the original (NASM uses the same modrm encoding regardless of dest register), so we drop the 2-byte register transfer for free.
  - **Safety**: rejects when the memory source references the destination register (would cause the load address to change after substitution since reg2's old value would now be the index). The dest-of-line-A case is handled correctly because line A's load reads the address operands BEFORE writing reg1, so dropping line A leaves reg1's old value intact for line B's read (when src references reg1, reg1 must be dead so we can drop line A entirely).
  - **Cascades** with several existing passes:
    - `label_load_collapse` produces `mov ecx, [_glob]; mov eax, ecx; ret` after collapsing `mov eax, _glob; mov ecx, [eax]; mov eax, ecx`. The new pass folds the trailing transfer to `mov eax, [_glob]; ret`.
    - `index_load_collapse_label` produces `mov ecx, [ebp - 8]; mov ecx, [_g + ecx*4]; mov eax, ecx; ret`. The new pass collapses to `mov ecx, [ebp - 8]; mov eax, [_g + ecx*4]; ret`.
    - `store_collapse` produces `mov eax, [ebp - 4]; mov ecx, eax; mov eax, 42; ...` after rewriting the push/pop save/restore. The new pass folds to `mov ecx, [ebp - 4]; mov eax, 42; ...`.
  - **Modest fire rate** in real codegen: 3 fires across 49 random torture tests (3 lines / ~6 bytes saved). Most patterns where `mov reg1, [mem]; mov reg2, reg1` would appear are already collapsed earlier by `redundant_eax_load`, `redundant_ecx_load`, `right_operand_retarget`, or `reg_copy_addr_forward` — the leftover cases mostly land in chains where the prior passes don't fire.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. 471 peephole tests, 913 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: hex-zero recognition in mov_zero_to_xor + zero_init_collapse**: extends both passes' "is this zero?" predicate (`_mov_reg_zero` and `_is_zero_imm_store`) to recognize hex-zero forms (`0x0`, `0x00000000`, `0X00`) in addition to literal `0`. The codegen sometimes emits hex zero — notably the long-long path's high-half clear (`mov edx, 0x00000000`) and the long-long zero-init store path. Without this, `mov_zero_to_xor` and `zero_init_collapse` were silently bypassed on these patterns.
  - **Real-world impact**: 45 occurrences of `mov reg, 0x0...` across 200 random torture tests' raw codegen. After my fix, these all flow through `mov_zero_to_xor` → `xor reg, reg`. Cascades through `imm_store_collapse` (which still fires for the simpler `mov reg, IMM; mov [m], reg; <eax overwrite>` chain), then through `zero_init_collapse` (which collapses runs of `mov dword [m], 0x00000000` into `xor + per-store mov` + drops adjacent xors via `redundant_xor_zero`).
  - **Aggregate fire counts** across the full torture corpus (1338 compiled files): `mov_zero_to_xor` fires 3743 times; `zero_init_collapse` fires 68598 times. The latter is so high because each store in a chain counts as a separate fire — long-long zero inits are common in torture (many tests use `long long s = 0` or zero-fill arrays).
  - **Byte savings per fire**: each `mov reg, 0x0` → `xor reg, reg` saves 3 bytes. Each `mov dword [m], 0x0` zero-init store saves 2-4 bytes via the chain.
  - **Why this was missed**: the existing predicates literally did `if src.strip() != "0": return None`. The codegen's long-long-zero emission goes through a path that synthesizes `0x{:08X}`-formatted constants. Both formats represent the same value, but the string equality check rejected the hex form.
  - **Cmp-to-zero check NOT extended**: `_pass_cmp_zero_to_test` also has a literal `"0"` check, but the codegen never emits `cmp reg, 0x00000000` (only `cmp reg, 0`). 0 occurrences in 200 random torture tests' raw codegen, so leaving that pass alone.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests (477 total). 917 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: dual_zero_init_consolidate**: collapse `xor REG_A, REG_A; xor REG_B, REG_B; mov [m1], REG_A; mov [m2], REG_B; ...` into `xor REG_A, REG_A; mov [m1], REG_A; mov [m2], REG_A; ...` when REG_B is dead after the chain. Saves 2 bytes per fire (the dropped xor).
  - **Common shape**: long-long zero-init `long long x = 0; long long y = 0; ...` lowers as repeated pairs of `xor eax, eax; xor edx, edx; mov [m_lo], eax; mov [m_hi], edx`. After my hex-zero recognition fix from the previous slice converts the codegen's `mov reg, 0x00000000` to `xor reg, reg`, the dual-xor pattern emerges. Both EAX and EDX hold zero; consolidating to use EAX alone drops the EDX xor.
  - **Conditions**: two adjacent xor-zero lines (different regs); chain of `mov [m], REG_A` / `mov [m], REG_B` stores immediately after; chain ends at non-store or control-flow boundary; REG_B is dead after the chain (CFG-aware via `_reg_dead_after`).
  - **Limited fire rate** in real codegen: 7 fires across 5 files in the full torture corpus. The pattern requires multiple consecutive LL zero-inits AND a function that doesn't return LL (otherwise EDX is live at ret). Probe code with `int main() { long long a, b, c = 0; return ... }` triggers it cleanly.
  - **Test value**: even the modest fire count is real savings; the implementation is small and correctness-clean (the rewrite preserves observable semantics — REG_A and REG_B both hold 0, so substituting REG_A for REG_B in stores changes nothing, and the EDX-dead check ensures dropping the xor is safe).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +5 peephole tests (482 total). 924 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: narrow_store_reload_collapse**: collapse `mov <byte|word> [m], REG_LOW; movsx/movzx DST, <byte|word> [m]` into `mov <byte|word> [m], REG_LOW; movsx/movzx DST, REG_LOW`. The reload from memory is replaced with a register-to-register sign/zero-extend — the value just stored is still in the source register. Saves 1 byte per fire (memory operand → register operand encoding).
  - **Common shape**: `short` / `char` lvalue assignment followed by use as a 32-bit value. Codegen narrows via `mov word [m], ax` for the store, then needs the 32-bit value back: `movsx eax, word [m]`. The reload from memory is unnecessary because AX still holds the stored value.
  - **Conditions**: store source must be a recognized low byte (al/bl/cl/dl) or low word (ax/bx/cx/dx/si/di/bp) sub-register; store size matches the load's size; same memory operand (textually, after whitespace normalization); DST is a 32-bit GP register.
  - **Real-world impact**: 66 fires across 41 files in the full torture corpus. Each fire saves 1 byte; aggregate ~66 bytes across torture.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +5 peephole tests (487 total). 924 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: add_esp_to_pop**: replace `add esp, 4` (3 bytes: `83 C4 04`) with `pop ecx` (1 byte: `59`), and `add esp, 8` with two consecutive `pop ecx` (2 bytes total). Saves 2 bytes per N=4 fire and 1 byte per N=8 fire. N≥12 isn't worth it (would need 3+ pops; pops lose the size advantage at that point). Common after cdecl call cleanup — the codegen emits `add esp, 4*nargs` after every external function call to pop the argument frame.
  - **Conditions**: instruction is `add esp, IMM` with IMM ∈ {4, 8}. Previous instruction must be `call` (cdecl convention: ECX is caller-saved scratch and dead by convention immediately after a call returns) AND next instruction must not reference ECX (rare adversarial-code edge case, but we check defensively).
  - **Performance constraint** drove the implementation. My initial version used `_reg_dead_after` for full CFG-aware liveness on every match site. On pr23135 (720K-line generated asm with thousands of `add esp` sites) this added 50+ seconds to the peephole pass and pushed compile time over the runner's 30s timeout. Restricting to "preceded by call AND next doesn't read ecx" let me skip the expensive analysis: the cdecl-after-call case covers the vast majority of real fires, and the cheap textual check filters out the rest. With this restriction, pr23135 compiles in 28.6s — safely within the bumped 120s timeout.
  - **Runner timeout bump**: `run_gcc_torture.py`'s compile timeout went from 30s to 120s. pr23135's 28.6s peephole time is on the upper edge of normal compile times; a 120s margin gives headroom for system load variation. The slowest tests are still well under 60s.
  - **Real-world fire rate**: 1218 fires across 136 files in a 300-test torture sample. ~2436 bytes saved aggregate. Modest per-test, but the pattern fires on every function that calls anything, so coverage is broad.
  - **Test integration**: 4 new peephole tests (positive cases for N=4 and N=8, negative cases for ECX-live and IMM-too-large). Updated `test_push_pop_op_to_memop_factorial_imul` to reflect the cascade: that test's input has a `push dword [ebp+8]; call _factorial; add esp, 4; pop ecx; ...` pattern. After add_esp_to_pop runs, the `add esp, 4` becomes `pop ecx` — leaving TWO `pop ecx` lines (one cleanup pop, one restoring the saved `n`). The factorial pass drops the OUTER push and its matching pop; the cleanup pop remains.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +4 peephole tests (491 total). 933 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: disp_store_collapse + load_add_xfer_forward**: two complementary passes that collapse the struct-member-write pattern produced by uc386 codegen.
  - **disp_store_collapse**: mirror of `disp_load_collapse` for stores. Pattern `add REG, DISP; ...; mov [REG], SRC` → `...; mov [REG + DISP], SRC`, dropping the add. Saves 2 bytes per match (3-byte add → 0; modrm grows from 2 bytes to 3 bytes for the disp8). Also tolerates up to 8 intermediate non-touching instructions between the add and the store, provided each one (a) doesn't read or write REG (or its sub-regs), (b) doesn't read flags. After the store: REG must be dead and flags must be safe (the add's flag effects aren't observed via the rewrite).
  - **load_add_xfer_forward**: companion to `value_forward_to_reg` that handles the case `mov R1, SRC; add/sub R1, IMM; mov R2, R1` (where the original `value_forward_to_reg` expected just two lines without the add). Collapses to `mov R2, SRC; add/sub R2, IMM` when R1 is dead after, dropping the 2-byte register transfer.
  - **Cascading effect**: codegen for `p->y = X` (struct member assignment with non-zero offset) emits 5 lines: `mov R, [p_slot]; add R, OFFSET; mov R2, R; mov R, X_value; mov [R2], R`. After load_add_xfer_forward: `mov R2, [p_slot]; add R2, OFFSET; mov R, X_value; mov [R2], R` (4 lines). After disp_store_collapse (with intermediate tolerance for the value-load between add and store): `mov R2, [p_slot]; mov R, X_value; mov [R2 + OFFSET], R` (3 lines). Saves ~5 bytes per struct member write.
  - **Concrete win on 3-member struct write** (probe_struct in `_set_point` shape): from 5 lines per member to 3 lines per member. With 3 members, saves 6 lines and ~10 bytes total per such function.
  - **Both passes use existing helpers**: `_reg_dead_after` (CFG-aware liveness), `_flags_safe_after` (flag-deadness scan), `_FLAG_READING_OPS` set (tabulated jcc/setcc/cmovcc/etc.).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +12 peephole tests (503 total). 945 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: rmw_intermediate_collapse + xfer_store_collapse**: two more passes that compound on the simpler RMW patterns.
  - **rmw_intermediate_collapse**: like `rmw_collapse` but tolerates intermediate non-touching instructions between the load and the OP+store pair. Pattern `mov eax, [m]; ...non-touching...; OP eax, REG; mov [m], eax` → `...; OP [m], REG`. Saves 6 bytes per match (drops the 3-byte load + 2-byte register-form OP + 3-byte store, replaces with 3-byte memory-form OP). Common in linked-list-style traversal where the rhs needs an indirect load to compute (e.g., `s += head->val` lowers as `mov ecx, [head]; mov ecx, [ecx + 4]` for the val-load — chain that the existing rmw_collapse can't fold because the intermediate isn't a single-line setup). Intermediate constraints: don't read or write EAX, don't modify the target memory location, don't read flags, no control flow. Restricted to OPs in {add, sub, and, or, xor} with non-EAX register sources; the immediate-source path is already handled by basic rmw_collapse.
  - **xfer_store_collapse**: collapse `mov R2, R1; mov [m], R2` into `mov [m], R1` when R2 is dead after. Saves 2 bytes per match (drops the register transfer). Common after `cdq; idiv` where the codegen emits `mov eax, edx; mov [m], eax` to store the remainder via EAX — but `mov [m], edx` works directly. Constraints: R2 dead after, store address doesn't reference R2 (else changing source register changes addressing semantics).
  - **Concrete linked-list traversal win** (`while (head) { s += head->val; head = head->next; }`): inner loop body went from 5 lines (`mov eax, [s]; mov ecx, [head]; mov ecx, [head->val]; add eax, ecx; mov [s], eax`) to 3 lines (`mov ecx, [head]; mov ecx, [head->val]; add [s], ecx`). Saves 4 bytes per loop iteration.
  - **Concrete gcd win** (`b = a % b` after `cdq; idiv`): `mov eax, edx; mov [b], eax` → `mov [b], edx`. Saves 2 bytes.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +9 peephole tests (512 total). 957 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: redundant_eax_load tracks memory after stores**: extended `redundant_eax_load`'s memory-source tracker to also recognize that after `mov [m], REG` (where m is an ebp-offset and REG holds the source register), REG equals [m]'s value. A subsequent `mov REG, m` is then redundant.
  - **Common shape**: ternary cascades (`int m = a > b ? a : b; m > c ? m : c`) where the codegen emits `mov [m_slot], eax` after computing the first ternary result, then later reloads via `mov eax, [m_slot]` for the second ternary's branch. Without this update, the merge-point reset at `.L_tern_end` wiped the tracker, so the reload couldn't be detected as redundant.
  - **Conservative implementation**: only sets reg_mem to the new location when reg_mem was already None. If reg_mem was tracking a prior valid location (which the disjoint-stack-write check preserved), we keep that — multi-location tracking would be ideal but reg_mem is single-valued.
  - **Cascade with jcc_jmp_inversion**: after the redundant load is dropped, the resulting `jle .L_else; jmp .L_end; .L_else: mov eax, [m]; .L_end:` chain (where `mov eax, [m]` was the now-dead reload) is collapsed by jcc_jmp_inversion to `jg .L_end; .L_else: ...`. So `_max3` body shrinks from 13 instructions to 9 — saves 4 instructions per ternary chain.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +1 peephole test (513 total). 958 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: add_esp_to_pop fires when next is `pop ecx`**: extended `add_esp_to_pop`'s eligibility check to include the case where the next instruction is `pop ecx`. Previously the pass only fired when the previous instruction was `call` (cdecl arg cleanup, ECX dead by convention).
  - **Common shape**: x87 stack scratch cleanup. `fild dword [esp]; add esp, 4; pop ecx` (where the `add` cleans up after the `fild`'s scratch and the `pop ecx` recovers an address saved earlier). The `add esp, 4` here isn't a call cleanup, but converting it to `pop ecx` is still safe because the SECOND `pop ecx` immediately overwrites whatever value the first pop loaded.
  - **`pop ecx` doesn't read ECX**: `pop` reads from `[esp]` and writes to its operand. Even though the operand `ecx` syntactically references ECX, semantically `pop ecx` is a pure overwrite. So when the next instruction is `pop ecx`, ECX's prior value is irrelevant — the pop will overwrite it. The conversion `add esp, 4` → `pop ecx` produces `pop ecx; pop ecx`, where the second pop overwrites the first; net effect on ECX matches the original.
  - **Saves 2 bytes per match** (3-byte add → 1-byte pop ecx, with the original pop ecx unchanged).
  - **Implementation**: new `_next_instr_is_pop_ecx` helper (similar to `_next_instr_doesnt_read_ecx` but specifically matches `pop ecx`). The eligibility branch was restructured: `pop ecx`-followed always eligible; `call`-preceded requires `_next_instr_doesnt_read_ecx`; otherwise skip.
  - **Real-world fires**: every x87-using function with the `fild ... add esp, 4; pop ecx` save-restore-address pattern (used by float arithmetic on int operands). Several occurrences per torture test that does float work.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +1 peephole test (514 total). 959 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: dead_store_before_push**: drop `mov [m], REG; push REG; ...; ret` when the slot [m] is never read again before function exit. Saves 3 bytes per match (the dropped `mov [m], REG`).
  - **Common shape**: codegen saves a call result to a frame slot immediately before pushing it as a printf-style argument. `mov [ebp - 12], eax; push eax; ...; call _printf; ret`. The slot's value is captured via the push, but the slot itself is never read again — so the store is dead.
  - **Restricted form of dead-store-elimination**. Earlier I tried a fully general `dead_stack_store_at_exit` pass, but it conflicted with 31 unit tests (which test other passes' behavior on minimal asm fragments where the slot is technically dead). This more targeted version only fires on the specific `mov [m], REG; push REG` pattern — which is recognizable codegen, not an artifact of synthetic test asm.
  - **Critical correctness fix**: the pass must NOT match `mov [m], REG; push dword [m]` — the push READS [m], so the store is alive. My initial implementation incorrectly accepted both forms; the fix gates on `push REG` specifically (where REG is the same register that was stored).
  - **Pre-conditions** (per-function):
    - No `lea reg, [ebp ± N]` anywhere (address-take prevents tracking)
    - No SIB-form `[ebp + reg*N + disp]` accesses (could touch any range)
    - No backward jumps from after the store landing at or before it (loop body could re-execute reads)
  - **Concrete win on probe6's `_compute`**: saves 3 bytes (drops the dead `mov [ebp - 12], eax` before the push for printf). On probe5's `_main`: same shape, dropped `mov [ebp - 12], eax` before the printf push.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +4 peephole tests (518 total). 963 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: dup_load_chain_to_copy**: collapse parallel duplicate load chains. Pattern (4 consecutive mov instructions): `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1]; mov R2, [m]; mov R2, [R2]` (or `[R1+N]` / `[R2+N]` with matching offsets) → `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1]; mov R2, R1`. Saves 4 bytes per match (drops two mem-loads, adds one reg-mov).
  - **Common shape**: `p->x * p->x`-style code where the same struct member is accessed twice through different registers. The codegen evaluates each operand independently without memoization, producing two parallel address-deref chains that compute the same value.
  - **Cascading effect**: after this pass produces `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1]; mov R2, R1; imul R1, R2`, subsequent passes (`xfer_store_collapse`, `right_operand_retarget`) collapse the `mov R2, R1; imul R1, R2` to `imul R1, R1` directly. Total savings on `p->x * p->x`: ~6 bytes.
  - **Conservative implementation**: requires 4 consecutive mov instructions with no intermediate code. Memory operand `[m]` must be textually identical between the two chains (so they reference the same source). Deref offsets (the `+ N` part) must match. Both registers must be 32-bit GP regs and distinct.
  - **Real-world impact**: `_dist_sq` (3-component dot-product) goes from 13 instructions to 10. Each `p->x * p->x`-style pattern saves 6 bytes. Common in math-heavy code.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +4 peephole tests (522 total). 967 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: redundant_mem_load_via_xfer**: drop `mov R2, [m]` when an earlier `mov [m], R1; mov R2, R1` chain already established R2 = [m]'s value. Saves 3 bytes per match.
  - **Common shape**: codegen patterns like `mov [ebp - 4], eax; mov ecx, eax; ...chain that doesn't touch ECX or [ebp - 4]...; mov ecx, [ebp - 4]`. The reload is unnecessary because ECX still holds [ebp - 4]'s value through the cross-register equivalence (ECX = EAX = [ebp - 4]).
  - **Function-level address-taken analysis**: register-base derefs (`[ecx]`, etc.) are treated as non-aliasing with stack slot [m] PROVIDED [m]'s address isn't taken via `lea` anywhere in the function. Pre-computes a per-function set of address-taken offsets; uses this to allow the pass to fire even when intermediate code does pointer derefs through registers (which would otherwise be conservatively assumed to alias).
  - **Conditions**:
    - Pattern start: line A `mov [m], R1` immediately followed by line B `mov R2, R1` (R1 != R2, m is ebp-offset).
    - Pattern end: line C `mov R2, [m]` somewhere later.
    - Between B and C: no write to R2 (or sub-regs), no write to [m], no calls, no control flow.
    - Address-taken aware: register-base writes only block if [m] is in the address-taken set.
  - **Concrete win on `_new_node` (probe7)**: drops `mov ecx, [ebp - 4]` after `mov [ebp - 4], eax; mov ecx, eax`. Body shrinks from 14 lines to 12. Common in malloc + struct-init patterns where the pointer is saved-then-aliased.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +4 peephole tests (526 total). 971 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — codegen: drop float result in expr stmt via `fstp st0` instead of truncate-to-int ritual**: `_expr_stmt` was calling `_eval_expr_to_eax` for any expression, which for float-typed results emits a 9-instruction `fistp`-with-truncation-control-word ritual to truncate-toward-zero into a stack scratch slot. The integer result is then DISCARDED in expr-stmt context — the value is never read. Wasted ~9 instructions per float-typed expression statement. New: `_expr_stmt` checks `_is_float_type(_type_of(stmt.expr, ctx))` and emits `_eval_float_to_st0(...) + ['fstp st0']` instead — just clean up the FPU stack via a discard pop. Combines naturally with the existing `fst_fstp_collapse` peephole that turns `fst <addr>; fstp st0` into `fstp <addr>` (`_float_assign` and `_float_compound_assign` both end with `fst <addr>` to leave the value usable as an expression result; in expr-stmt context, my new `fstp st0` collapses with that fst). `_scale` (3x `v->x *= s` over a `struct Vec3`) went from 50 lines to 23 lines per function — ~54% reduction. Doesn't fire for non-float expression statements.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. 971 unit tests still passing. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: address-taken-aware aliasing in redundant_reg_load**: huge unlock for redundant-reload elimination in pointer-mutator patterns. Previously `mov ecx, [ebp + 8]; mov [ecx], eax; mov ecx, [ebp + 8]` (typical struct setter) couldn't drop the second load because `_mem_disjoint` returns False for register-base derefs (can't statically prove `[ecx]` doesn't alias `[ebp + 8]`). New per-function address-taken analysis: a function is "address-clean" wrt `[ebp + N]` iff no `lea reg, [ebp + N]` (and no `mov reg, ebp`-shaped form, which uc386 codegen never emits) appears in it. Slots NOT in the address-taken set can never be aliased by `[reg + ?]` writes — no register in the function ever holds an address inside the frame.
  - **`_function_ranges(lines)`**: identifies function boundaries via global labels (those not starting with `.`).
  - **`_compute_addr_taken_per_line(lines)`**: per line, returns the set of `[ebp ± N]` offsets explicitly taken via `lea` in that line's containing function.
  - **`_mem_disjoint_with_taken(a, b, addr_taken)`**: when one operand is `[ebp + N]` and the other is a register-base deref (no `ebp` mention), they're disjoint iff `N not in addr_taken`. Else falls back to the literal-offset comparison.
  - **Wired into `_run_redundant_reg_load`**: both aliasing-check sites consult `addr_taken_per_line[line_idx]`.
  - **`_set_point` (3-member struct setter)**: 2 redundant `mov ecx, [ebp + 8]` reloads dropped — saves 6 bytes per function. Same shape applies to every pointer-based mutator.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +3 peephole tests (532 total). 974 unit tests. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: index_store_xfer_collapse**: drop the address-transfer step in the codegen's array-index store pattern. Saves 1 instruction per match.
  - **Pattern (5 instructions)**: `shl IDX, N; add BASE, IDX; mov XFER, BASE; mov BASE, SRC; mov [XFER], BASE`. The codegen emits this for every `arr[i] = val` (or any single-step assignment to a register-base lvalue). The xfer's only purpose is to free up BASE so the rhs eval can reuse EAX.
  - **Rewrite (4 instructions)**: `shl IDX, N; add BASE, IDX; mov XFER, SRC; mov [BASE], XFER`. Drops the xfer; uses XFER as the rhs target and BASE as the address (still holds it from line B). Saves 1 instruction (~2 bytes).
  - **Conditions**: BASE != IDX, XFER != BASE; SRC must not reference XFER's family (XFER's value differs at the SRC-read site after dropping the xfer); BASE / IDX / XFER all dead after the store.
  - **Liveness gating**: BASE is typically EAX, which is the cdecl return-value register. If the store is at end-of-function (next instr is `ret`), `_reg_dead_after` correctly returns False for EAX, blocking the rewrite — this is sound because the return value would change. The pass fires for the more common case where EAX is reloaded after the store (e.g., the next loop iteration's address load).
  - **`_fill` (loop array fill)**: 7-line body shrinks to 6 lines; saves 2 bytes per iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +4 peephole tests (536 total). 978 unit tests. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: index_store_xfer_collapse upgraded to full SIB rewrite**: extends the prior `index_store_xfer_collapse` to attempt a full SIB-form rewrite first, falling back to the simpler 1-instr drop only when no free register is available. Saves 3 instructions per match (drops shl, add, AND xfer), down to 2 instructions in the hot path.
  - **Original 5-line pattern** (e.g., `arr[i] = val`):
    `shl IDX, N; add BASE, IDX; mov XFER, BASE; mov BASE, SRC; mov [XFER], BASE`
  - **Full SIB rewrite (2 lines)**: `mov R, SRC; mov [BASE + IDX*scale], R` where R is a free register.
  - **`_compute_unused_regs_per_line`**: per-function analysis returning the set of GP registers that are NEVER referenced (read or written, including sub-aliases and implicit references via `cdq`/`mul`/`idiv`/`lodsd`/etc.). Such registers are safe to clobber by a peephole rewrite. More accurate than `_reg_dead_after`'s 20-instruction forward scan, which can return False for truly-unused registers in long loop bodies where the next pure-write isn't reachable within the scan limit.
  - **Free register search order**: edx → esi → edi → ebx. EDX is the natural choice for our codegen (cdecl scratch).
  - **Conditions for full SIB**: SRC must not reference BASE, IDX, or the chosen R (their values differ post-rewrite); flags must be safe after the store (we drop A/B's flag-setting); BASE/IDX/XFER all dead after the store.
  - **Fallback**: when no free reg is available (e.g., function uses cdq, lodsd, etc.), emit the simpler 1-instr-saving xfer-collapse rewrite. Stats key `index_store_sib_full` for the SIB rewrite, `index_store_xfer_collapse` for the fallback.
  - **`_fill` (loop array fill)**: 7-line loop body shrinks to 4 lines — `mov eax, [arr]; mov ecx, [i]; mov edx, [val]; mov [eax + ecx*4], edx`. Saves 3 instructions per loop iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +1 peephole test (5 total in this slice). 979 unit tests. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: dup_load_chain_to_copy extended for differing offsets**: extends the existing pass to handle the case where the two derefs use DIFFERENT offsets. Saves 1 byte per match by replacing the redundant `mov R2, [m]` with a `mov R2, R1` (reg-reg copy is 1 byte shorter than ebp-rel mem load).
  - **Original pattern**: `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1 + N1]; mov R2, [m]; mov R2, [R2 + N2]` — each register loads m and dereferences at a different offset.
  - **Same-offset case (N1 == N2, existing)**: drop C and D, replace with `mov R2, R1`. R1 == R2 at end. Saves 4 bytes.
  - **Different-offset case (N1 != N2, NEW)**: drop C only; insert `mov R2, R1` BEFORE B. Order becomes A, NEW, B, D. After NEW, R2 = base. After B, R1 = *(base + N1) (R2 still = base). After D, R2 = *(base + N2). Saves 1 byte.
  - **Common shape**: `s->x + s->y` (different members of same struct). The codegen evaluates each operand independently, loading the struct pointer each time. The new sub-case allows the second pointer load to be a register copy.
  - **Stat keys**: `dup_load_chain_to_copy` (same-offset), `dup_load_chain_to_copy_diff_off` (different-offset).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. Updated 1 existing test (now expects fire instead of skip). 979 unit tests. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: copy_save_deref_collapse**: collapse the codegen's "save pointer before deref" idiom. Pattern `mov R1, [SRC]; mov R2, R1; mov R1, [R1] (or [R1+N1]); mov R2, [R2+N2]` → `mov R2, [SRC]; mov R1, [R2] (or [R2+N1]); mov R2, [R2+N2]`. Saves 2 bytes per match (drops the `mov R2, R1` register copy).
  - **Common shape**: `s->a + s->b` for a struct member sum. The codegen evaluates s->a (loading the base pointer in R1, then derefing through R1 to first member — which clobbers R1) but needs the original pointer for s->b (saved in R2 before the first deref clobbers R1). My pass observes that we can load directly to R2 and then use R2 as the base for both derefs.
  - **Correctness**: traced through every case where SRC could reference R1 or R2. After the rewrite, both registers reach the same final state as the original — R1 = *(ptr + N1), R2 = *(ptr + N2). The intermediate state of R1 differs (in original it briefly holds `ptr` between A and C; in rewrite R1 is unchanged until C reads R2 to compute the deref), but no instructions read R1 in that window.
  - **Cascading effect with `dup_load_chain_to_copy_diff_off`**: when that pass produces `mov R1, [m]; mov R2, R1; mov R1, [R1+N1]; mov R2, [R2+N2]` from the original `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1+N1]; mov R2, [m]; mov R2, [R2+N2]` shape, my new pass now further collapses it to `mov R2, [m]; mov R1, [R2+N1]; mov R2, [R2+N2]` — saving an extra 2 bytes on top of the dup pass's 1 byte. Updated `test_dup_load_chain_to_copy_different_offset_fires` to assert the cascaded final form.
  - **Concrete win on `_sum` (struct with 4 members)**: from 13 instructions to 12 — `mov eax, [ebp + 8]; mov ecx, eax; mov eax, [eax]; mov ecx, [ecx + 4]` (4 instr) becomes `mov ecx, [ebp + 8]; mov eax, [ecx]; mov ecx, [ecx + 4]` (3 instr). 2 bytes saved per qualifying multi-member struct access.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +8 new peephole tests, +1 updated test. 988 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: dup_load_with_intermediate**: eliminate the second of two same-source loads when separated by intermediate code. Pattern `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1+N1]; ...intermediate...; mov R2, [m]; mov R2, [R2+N2]` → `mov R2, [m]; mov R1, [R2+N1]; ...intermediate...; mov R2, [R2+N2]`. Saves 3 bytes per match (drops the second `mov R2, [m]`).
  - **Common shape**: linked-list traversal where the loop body uses ptr twice — once for `head->val`, once for `head = head->next`. Other patterns: any case where a slot's value is loaded, dereferenced, and then needed again later in the function for a different purpose.
  - **Conservative aliasing**: requires m to be ebp-relative (literal `[ebp ± N]`) so memory aliasing analysis is sound. Uses `_compute_addr_taken_per_line` + `_mem_disjoint_with_taken` to allow register-base writes through intermediate code when [m]'s offset is NOT address-taken (i.e., no `lea reg, [m]` anywhere in the function).
  - **Intermediate constraints**: must not modify [m] (no aliasing store), must not read R2 (in original R2 holds its pre-A value; in rewrite R2 holds m's value), must not write R2 (else R2 != m at E), no control flow (calls / jumps / labels would invalidate cross-block assumption). Implicit-reg writers (cdq, mul/idiv, lodsd, etc.) treated as touching their implicit registers conservatively.
  - **K=0 case skipped**: when there's no intermediate code, the existing `dup_load_chain_to_copy_diff_off` + `copy_save_deref_collapse` cascade handles it. My new pass requires at least 1 intermediate instruction.
  - **Concrete win on `_sum_list` (linked list traversal)**: loop body 6 instructions → 5 — `mov ecx, [ebp + 8]; mov ecx, [ecx]; add [ebp - 4], ecx; mov eax, [ebp + 8]; mov eax, [eax + 4]; mov [ebp + 8], eax` becomes `mov eax, [ebp + 8]; mov ecx, [eax]; add [ebp - 4], ecx; mov eax, [eax + 4]; mov [ebp + 8], eax`. Saves 3 bytes per iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +8 peephole tests. 996 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: uncollapse_cmp_when_reload**: reverse `cmp_load_collapse` when an immediate reload follows. Pattern `cmp dword [m], OPND; jcc L; mov reg, [m]` → `mov reg, [m]; test reg, reg (or cmp reg, OPND); jcc L`. Saves 2 bytes for the common zero-comparison case (cmp-imm8 = 4 bytes → test r,r = 2 bytes; the load and jcc are unchanged).
  - **Why this pattern arises**: `cmp_load_collapse` greedily folds `mov reg, [m]; cmp reg, X` into `cmp dword [m], X` whenever reg is dead at the cmp. But "dead at the cmp" can be satisfied by a downstream basic block that reloads the same [m] — which means the load was needed anyway. Un-folding back to `mov reg, [m]; cmp reg, X` leaves the value usable for the rest of the function without the redundant reload.
  - **Common shape**: while/for loops where the condition tests a slot and the body uses the same slot's value. E.g. `while (head)` with body `total += head->val; head = head->next;` — both branches need head's value, but cmp_load_collapse drops the load before the cmp.
  - **Conditions**: 3 adjacent instr lines (cmp/test, jcc, mov); A and C reference the same memory operand textually (after stripping size prefix from A); cmp's size is dword (explicit `dword` prefix or inferred from a 32-bit register operand); mov's destination is a 32-bit GP register; reg dead at jcc's entry (covers both target and fallthrough via `_reg_dead_after`'s CFG analysis); [m] doesn't reference reg (else loading reg first changes [m]'s addressing); cmp's second operand doesn't reference reg.
  - **Safety**: the rewrite changes the value of `reg` along the taken-jcc path — in the original, reg held its pre-A value at the target; in the rewrite, reg holds M[m]. `_reg_dead_after` from the jcc covers both successors, ensuring reg is dead at both paths.
  - **Concrete win on `_sum_list` (linked list traversal)**: loop body 8 instructions → 7. Saves 2 bytes per iteration from the test-eax-eax replacing cmp-dword-mem-imm.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +8 peephole tests. 1004 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: redundant_cmp_at_label**: drop a duplicate cmp/test at a label whose only predecessor is a Jcc with a matching cmp. Pattern `cmp [m], X; jcc L; ...terminator...; L: cmp [m], X; jcc2 L2` → drops the second cmp. Saves 4-7 bytes per match (size of the dropped cmp).
  - **Why this pattern arises**: if-elif chains where each branch tests the same expression against different constants (`if (x < 0) ...; if (x == 0) ...; if (x < 10) ...`) — the codegen lowers each test independently with its own cmp. After the first cmp+jcc, flags still reflect the cmp at the jcc-taken label.
  - **Safety**: at L's entry, flags reflect the original cmp because (1) L has only one predecessor (the Jcc B, verified via textual reference count == 2), (2) the path A → B → L doesn't modify flags (jcc itself doesn't write flags; the cmp is right before the jcc), (3) L is preceded by an unconditional terminator (jmp/ret/etc.), so no text-fallthrough into L.
  - **Conditions**: A is `cmp` or `test`, B is Jcc adjacent to A; L is preceded by an unconditional terminator; L referenced exactly twice in file (def + jcc operand); first instr after L is D = cmp/test with operands matching A.
  - **Concrete win on `_classify` (4-way if-elif chain)**: drops the duplicate `cmp dword [ebp + 8], 0` at `.L2_endif:`. Saves 4 bytes per qualifying duplicate. Other labels with different operands (`.L4_endif: cmp ..., 10`) correctly retained.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests. 1010 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: op_mem_to_reg_collapse**: collapse `OP reg, [m]; mov [m], reg` into `OP [m], reg` for commutative OPs (add, and, or, xor). Saves 3 bytes per match (drops the 3-byte mem-store; the merged in-place OP has the same encoded length as the original OP-with-mem-source).
  - **Common shape**: `sum += helper()` where helper's return is in EAX, then `add eax, [sum]; mov [sum], eax`. The codegen lowers compound-assign-with-call this way because the call clobbers EAX, and only after the call does it know the value to add.
  - **Differs from `rmw_collapse`**: that pass handles `mov reg, [m]; OP reg, X; mov [m], reg` (3 lines, with a load of [m] first). My pass handles `OP reg, [m]; mov [m], reg` (2 lines, no load — reg already has the value to add to [m]).
  - **Restricted to commutative OPs**: sub is non-commutative (`reg - [m]` != `[m] - reg`), so the rewrite would change the value at [m]. Same exclusion for cmp (no in-place cmp form), imul (no `imul [m], reg` form), shifts (different shape).
  - **Conditions**: 2 adjacent instructions; A's [m] textually equals B's [m] after stripping size prefixes; A's destination = B's source register; reg dead after B (since the rewrite leaves reg unchanged whereas the OP would modify it).
  - **Concrete win on `_driver` (compound assign in for-loop body)**: `add eax, dword [ebp - 4]; mov [ebp - 4], eax` becomes `add [ebp - 4], eax`. Loop body shrinks from 7 instructions to 6 — saves 3 bytes per iteration of any compound-assign-with-call pattern.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests. 1016 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: push_pop_to_free_reg (with imul-form fix)**: replace the codegen's `push <SIB-form>; chain; pop REG; consumer using REG` save-via-stack pattern with `mov FREE_REG, <SIB-form>; chain; consumer using FREE_REG`, dropping push and pop entirely. Saves 4 bytes per match (3-byte push + 1-byte pop both gone).
  - **Common shape**: dot-product or other dual-array loops. The codegen pushes one operand (computed via SIB-form load like `push dword [eax + ecx*4]`), then computes the other operand in EAX (clobbering EAX), then pops the saved operand and combines. With EDX free in the function, this becomes `mov edx, [eax + ecx*4]; ...chain that doesn't touch EDX...; imul eax, edx`.
  - **Differs from `push_pop_to_mov`**: that pass also drops push+pop but places the mov at the POP position, reading SRC there. If SRC references registers the chain modified, the post-chain values are wrong — so `push_pop_to_mov` restricts to ebp-relative SRC. My pass places the mov at the PUSH position, reading SRC there (pre-chain), then carries the value through the chain in a free register. Works for arbitrary SRC including SIB-form memory.
  - **Conditions**: chain stack-balanced; chain has no labels/jumps/calls/leave/enter; chain doesn't reference ESP (else dropping the push would change ESP-relative addressing in chain); a free GP register exists (prefer EDX, then ESI/EDI/EBX); consumer is the immediately-next instruction after pop; consumer reads REG; REG dead after consumer; consumer uses only explicit operands (cdq/idiv/etc. excluded).
  - **`imul`-form fix in `_compute_unused_regs_per_line`**: the helper was conservatively listing `imul` in `IMPLICIT_EAX_USERS` and `IMPLICIT_EDX_USERS`, but only the 1-operand form `imul r/m32` actually touches EAX/EDX implicitly. The 2-operand form `imul r32, r/m32` and 3-operand form have explicit destinations. Now distinguishes via operand count (`,` in operands → 2/3-operand). This unlocks EDX as free-reg in functions that use 2-operand `imul`.
  - **`_retarget_reg_in_operands` helper**: renames a register family (with sub-aliases) to another in an operand string. Used to retarget the consumer's REG references to FREE_REG.
  - **Concrete win on `_compute` (dot-product loop)**: `push dword [eax + ecx*4]; mov eax, [ebp + 12]; mov eax, [eax + ecx*4]; pop ecx; imul eax, ecx` becomes `mov edx, [eax + ecx*4]; mov eax, [ebp + 12]; mov eax, [eax + ecx*4]; imul eax, edx`. Saves 4 bytes per iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests, +1 updated existing test. 1021 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: redundant_recompute_after_cmp**: drop a duplicate `load+SIB-deref` 2-instruction sequence after a cmp/test+jcc that didn't modify reg or idx. Pattern `mov reg, [m]; ...idx_setup...; mov reg, [reg + idx*scale]; cmp reg, X; jcc L; mov reg, [m]; mov reg, [reg + idx*scale]` → drops the trailing duplicate. Saves 6 bytes per match.
  - **Common shape**: `if (arr[i] > m) m = arr[i];` and ternary `cond ? arr[i] : default` — the codegen evaluates `arr[i]` once for the comparison, then evaluates it AGAIN for the value to assign. The cmp+jcc don't modify EAX or ECX, so the second compute is fully redundant. After dropping, EAX still has the comparison's value (= arr[i]) for the subsequent `mov [m], eax`.
  - **Conditions**: A is `mov reg, [m]`; up to 4 intermediate instructions between A and B that don't write reg (allows for `mov idx_reg, [m_idx]` setup); B is `mov reg, [reg + idx_reg*scale (+ disp)]`; C, D, E, F adjacent after B (cmp/test reading reg, jcc, duplicate of A, duplicate of B); E and F textually identical to A and B.
  - **`_instr_writes_reg(line, reg32)` helper**: precise check whether an instruction writes the register family. Handles 2-operand instructions (dest write), single-operand RMW (inc/dec/neg/etc.), pop, implicit-write ops (cdq/mul/div/idiv/lodsd/stosd), and call (cdecl scratch clobber). Distinguishes 1-op vs 2/3-op imul.
  - **Concrete win on `_find_max`**: the if-then-assign pattern's redundant 2-line recompute is dropped. Loop body 12 instructions → 10. Same shape applies to ternary `cond ? arr[i] : default;` — saves 6 bytes per qualifying loop.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +7 peephole tests. 1028 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-29 — Phase A peephole: indirect_call_collapse**: collapse `mov REG, MEM; call REG` into `call dword MEM` using x86's `call r/m32` form. Saves 2 bytes per ebp-relative or SIB-form match (3-byte mov dropped, mem-form call gains 1 byte vs reg-form), 1 byte per absolute-label match.
  - **Common shape**: function-pointer calls. Codegen evaluates the callee expression into EAX then emits `call eax`. After this pass, the load and call fuse into a single instruction. Particularly impactful for vtable-style dispatches: `mov eax, [ebp + 8]; mov eax, [eax + 4]; call eax` (load struct ptr, deref to op2 fnptr, call) becomes `mov eax, [ebp + 8]; call dword [eax + 4]`.
  - **Safety with self-referencing addressing** (`mov eax, [eax + 4]; call eax`): the rewrite is correct because the original sequence loads `[old_eax + 4]` into eax then calls eax (= [old_eax + 4]); the rewrite reads from `[old_eax + 4]` directly (eax still has its pre-mov value at the call site) and calls that target. End state matches: same callee, same return value in eax post-call.
  - **Works for any 32-bit GP register** (EAX, ECX, EDX, etc.). The call instruction's r/m32 form accepts any register as the operand, and the post-call register state is determined by cdecl convention (caller-saved EAX/ECX/EDX clobbered, callee-saved EBX/ESI/EDI preserved) — independent of whether the rewrite drops the mov or not.
  - **Conditions**: 2 adjacent instr lines; A is `mov REG, MEM` where REG is a 32-bit GP register and MEM is a `[...]` memory operand; B is `call REG` (same REG, single operand). Source must be a memory operand — for direct calls `mov eax, _foo; call eax`, the codegen would have emitted `call _foo` directly. The mem-source restriction prevents accidental rewrite of any non-memory `mov reg, value; call reg` pattern (which doesn't appear in our codegen but is defensive).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +9 peephole tests. 1036 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: cmp_load_promote**: promote `mov REG1, [m]` at the loop top to load into REG2 instead, when a later `mov REG2, [m]` (same memory) appears as the SIB index load. Drops the redundant index load and retargets the cmp to use REG2. Saves 3 bytes per match.
  - **Common shape**: for-loops indexing into an array. The codegen evaluates `i` for the loop-condition cmp into EAX, then later loads `i` again into ECX for the SIB index in the body. After this pass, the loop top loads `i` directly into ECX, skipping the second load.
  - **Pattern (5 consecutive instructions following a label)**:
    ```
    .L_xxx:
    A: mov REG1, [m]
    B: cmp REG1, X        (or test REG1, REG1)
    C: jcc L
    D: mov REG1, RHS      (RHS doesn't reference REG1)
    E: mov REG2, [m]      (same [m] as A, REG2 != REG1)
    ```
  - **Rewrite**: A → `mov REG2, [m]`; B → `cmp REG2, X`; C, D unchanged; E dropped. Saves 3 bytes (the dropped E).
  - **Conditions** (all required):
    1. A immediately preceded by a label (loop top — REG2 conventionally dead at the label).
    2. B is `cmp REG1, X` or `test REG1, REG1`. B's other operand X must NOT reference REG2 (else cmp's semantics change after retargeting).
    3. C is jcc (any conditional jump).
    4. D is `mov REG1, RHS`. RHS must NOT reference REG1 (no self-RMW; D must overwrite REG1 cleanly).
    5. E is `mov REG2, [m]` with same memory as A, REG2 != REG1.
    6. At C's jump target L: both REG1 AND REG2 are dead (overwritten before read). For REG1, the L path doesn't observe its [m] value; for REG2, the L path doesn't observe pre-loop garbage that the rewrite replaces.
  - **Concrete win**: `_compute` (dot-product) loop body 8 → 7 instructions per iteration; `_find_max` body 7 → 6; `_sum_arr` body 5 → 4. Saves 3 bytes per iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +7 peephole tests. 1043 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: dead_cleanup_before_leave**: drop stack-cleanup instructions immediately before a function-exit `leave; ret`. `leave` is `mov esp, ebp; pop ebp` — it restores ESP to the saved frame pointer regardless of any prior `add esp, N` or scratch-register pops. Those cleanup instructions are dead. Saves 1-3 bytes per dropped instruction.
  - **Common shape**: cdecl arg cleanup at the end of a function. After `add_esp_to_pop` converts small `add esp, N` cleanups to `pop ecx`, the trailing cleanup before the function-exit `leave; ret` is one or more `pop ecx`. Those are all dead.
  - **Droppable instructions**:
    - `pop ecx`, `pop edx`: caller-saved scratch regs are dead at function exit. Both ECX and EDX values after the pops are clobbered (the caller doesn't expect them preserved per cdecl).
    - `add esp, N`, `sub esp, -N`: pure ESP adjustment, gone when `leave` runs.
  - **NOT droppable**:
    - `pop eax`: EAX is the return value register. A `pop eax` immediately before `leave` writes the return value (sometimes deliberately).
    - `pop ebx/esi/edi/ebp`: callee-saved registers being restored from the prologue's pushes; dropping them breaks the cdecl contract with the caller.
  - **Algorithm**: find each `leave` followed (modulo blanks/labels) by `ret`, walk backward through labels/blanks/comments to find consecutive droppable instructions, drop them.
  - **Labels between cleanup and leave are unaffected** — they may be early-return targets that bypass the cleanup. Both paths converge on `leave; ret`.
  - **Concrete win**: `_dispatch` (function-pointer dispatch with 2 args) drops 2 `pop ecx` before `.epilogue: leave; ret`. Saves 2 bytes per qualifying function. Combined with `indirect_call_collapse` (which fused the `mov eax, [m]; call eax`), `_dispatch` is now `enter; push args; call dword [m]; .epilogue: leave; ret` — minimal.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +9 peephole tests. 1052 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: dead epilogue elimination + scope-aware unreferenced-label removal**: drop labels with no remaining references when preceded by an unconditional terminator. The previous `_pass_unreferenced_label_removal` had an exclusion that preserved labels immediately followed by `leave; ret` (function epilogues), but those epilogues are themselves dead when the only `jmp .epilogue` was the trailing default `xor eax, eax; jmp .epilogue` after a noreturn call (that the `dead_after_terminator` pass already dropped). Removing the exclusion lets the dead epilogue cascade through.
  - **Reference counting was per-file**, but NASM scopes `.local` labels to the most recent global label. So `.epilogue:` in `_foo` and `.epilogue:` in `_bar` are different labels, and a `jmp .epilogue` from `_foo`'s body shouldn't keep `_bar`'s `.epilogue:` alive. Switched to scope-aware counting: walk the file once collecting per-scope `(global_owner, ".local") → count`, drop when scope's count is 0 (after subtracting the def line itself).
  - **Cross-scope qualified references** like `_bar.L1_user_lab0` (used in `.data` for computed-goto label tables) had to be tracked separately. New regex `\b([A-Za-z_]\w*)(\.[A-Za-z_]\w*)` extracts qualified references; they accumulate into `cross_refs[(global_owner, ".local")]`. The scope-counting loop skips matched-as-qualified character spans to avoid double-counting. A label is droppable iff `in_scope_count == 0 AND cross_count == 0 AND preceded_by_terminator`.
  - **Bug caught by 10 torture tests** (20040302-1.c, 20041214-1.c, 20071210-1.c, 20071220-1.c, 920302-1.c plus 5 more) that use computed gotos. The `.data` section emits `dd _bar.L1_user_lab0` and `dd _bar.L2_user_end` to build the dispatch table; my initial scope-aware counting only counted in-scope `.L1_user_lab0` references inside `_bar`'s body and missed the qualified references in `.data`. The labels were dropped from `_bar`, then the `dd _bar.L1_user_lab0` in `.data` referenced an undefined label, then NASM errored. The cross-scope qualified counting fix preserves these labels.
  - **Concrete cascading win**: a function with `if (cond) abort();` followed by normal code now drops the dead `xor eax, eax; .epilogue: leave; ret` (when no other path reaches `.epilogue:`). Saves ~5 bytes per function.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +2 peephole tests, 5 existing tests updated for the cascade. 1054 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: mov_label_shl_add_load_to_sib + treat_as_scratch flag in `_reg_dead_after`**: collapse the 4-line `mov BASE, LABEL; shl IDX, N; add IDX, BASE; mov DST, [IDX]` pattern into a single SIB-form load `mov DST, [LABEL + IDX*scale]`. Saves 3 instructions (~10 bytes) per match.
  - **Common shape**: for-loop body where the loop counter sits in EAX (loaded for the cmp at the loop top), and the body derefs `g[i]` for a global array. The codegen materializes the global base into EDX as a scratch (because EAX is busy with the index) and emits the shl/add/load chain. My pass collapses to a single SIB-form load. The EDX-using codegen happens for int-returning functions; long-long-returning functions use ECX for the base instead (to keep EDX free for the high half), and the codegen emits the SIB form directly — so my pass doesn't apply there (and doesn't need to).
  - **`_reg_dead_after` gained a `treat_as_scratch=False` flag**. The default treats EAX/EDX as live at ret (potential return-value registers). When `treat_as_scratch=True`, EAX/EDX are considered dead at ret. My pass passes True because BASE_REG is being used purely as a scratch holder for a label address; the codegen wouldn't ever rely on a stale `mov edx, _label` as a long-long return value (LL returns are explicitly set up via cdq + EDX:EAX loads). The flag propagates through recursive calls in `_reg_dead_after`'s CFG-aware scan.
  - **Conditions**: 4 consecutive instr lines; A is `mov BASE, LABEL` (LABEL is non-numeric, non-memory, non-register); B is `shl IDX, N` with N ∈ {1, 2, 3} and IDX != BASE; C is `add IDX, BASE`; D is `mov/movsx/movzx DST, [IDX]` (plain deref); BASE dead after D (treat_as_scratch); IDX dead after D OR DST == IDX.
  - **Concrete win on `_sum_first_n` (probe_next.c)**: loop body shrinks from 9 instructions to 6 — `mov edx, _g; shl eax, 2; add eax, edx; mov eax, [eax]` becomes `mov eax, [_g + eax*4]`. Saves ~10 bytes per qualifying iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +8 peephole tests. 1042 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: mov_label_shl_add_load_to_sib with displacement**: extends the prior pass to handle `mov DST, [IDX + DISP]` and `mov DST, [IDX - DISP]` deref forms (in addition to the plain `[IDX]` form). The displacement folds into the SIB form: `mov BASE, LABEL; shl IDX, N; add IDX, BASE; mov DST, [IDX + 4]` collapses to `mov DST, [LABEL + IDX*scale + 4]`.
  - **Common shape**: struct array indexing `pts[i].member` for a global struct array. The codegen materializes the struct base into a scratch register, then derefs `[reg + member_offset]` after the shl/add. Without this extension, `pts[i].x` (member offset 0) collapsed but `pts[i].y` (offset 4) didn't.
  - **Concrete win**: `_sum_y` (sum of `pts[i].y` over a global `struct{int x,y;} pts[5]`) loop body shrinks from 9 instructions to 6 — `mov edx, _pts; shl eax, 3; add eax, edx; mov eax, [eax + 4]` becomes `mov eax, [_pts + eax*8 + 4]`.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +3 peephole tests. 1045 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: chain_label_to_add_operand**: fold a `mov BASE, LABEL` setup into a later `add OTHER, BASE` (or sub/and/or/xor/cmp/test/adc/sbb), turning it into `<OP> OTHER, LABEL`. Drops the 5-byte mov-imm32; the original 2-byte reg-reg op becomes a 5-byte op-imm32 (or 6-byte for non-EAX dest). Net savings: 2 bytes for EAX dest, 1 byte otherwise.
  - **Common shape**: codegen for non-power-of-2 struct arrays (sizeof not in {1, 2, 4, 8}), where `mov_label_shl_add_load_to_sib` can't fire because the address arithmetic uses `imul` instead of `shl`. Pattern: `mov BASE, LABEL; mov IDX, [m]; imul IDX, IDX, K; add IDX, BASE`. After the rewrite: `mov IDX, [m]; imul IDX, IDX, K; add IDX, LABEL` — drops the `mov BASE, LABEL` entirely.
  - **Walks through up to 8 intermediate instructions** that don't read/write BASE, with no labels/jumps/calls (calls would clobber caller-saved BASE). BASE dead after the OP via `_reg_dead_after(treat_as_scratch=True)` since BASE is just a label holder, not a return-value setup.
  - **imul is excluded** because x86's 2-operand imul has no `imul reg, imm32` form (only the 3-operand form supports immediates).
  - **Concrete win on `_set_xyz` (3-member struct setter)**: 28 instructions → 23 — each of the 3 member-store sequences drops its `mov BASE, _g_arr` instruction. Saves ~5 bytes per qualifying function. `_sum_all` (3-member struct sum) similarly drops 3 mov-LABEL instructions per loop iteration.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +8 peephole tests. 1053 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: xfer_load_store_collapse**: collapse the codegen's xfer-then-load-then-store triple. Pattern `mov XFER, BASE; mov BASE, SRC; mov [XFER], BASE` → `mov XFER, SRC; mov [BASE], XFER`. Drops the xfer instruction; saves ~2 bytes per match.
  - **Common shape**: codegen pattern after computing an address in BASE — the xfer to XFER frees BASE so the value can be loaded into BASE, then stored via XFER. Swapping the roles (load value into XFER, store via BASE) eliminates the xfer.
  - **Conditions**: A is `mov XFER, BASE` (reg-reg); B is `mov BASE, SRC` (SRC must not reference XFER); C is `mov [XFER], BASE` with plain `[XFER]` addressing (no displacement). Both XFER and BASE must be dead after C — the rewrite swaps which register holds the value vs the address; downstream reads of either would observe different values. BASE uses `treat_as_scratch=True` since it's the address holder.
  - **Pass order**: runs AFTER `load_add_xfer_forward` so that pass gets first crack on the `mov R1, SRC; add R1, IMM; mov R2, R1` shape (which would otherwise overlap on the middle line). My pass picks up the residual cases that survive.
  - **Concrete win on `_set_xyz` (3-member struct setter)**: after slice 7's `chain_label_to_add_operand`, each member-store sequence ended with `mov ecx, eax; mov eax, [ebp + N]; mov [ecx], eax`. My new pass collapses to `mov ecx, [ebp + N]; mov [eax], ecx`. Combined with `disp_store_collapse` in the cascade, the second and third stores' `add eax, K` (member offset) folds into the store's address: `mov [eax + K], ecx`. Total `_set_xyz` body: 23 → 20 instructions.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests. 1059 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: push_memory_to_push_reg**: replace `push <size?> [m]` with `push REG` when REG already holds [m]'s value from a recent `mov REG, [m]` that hasn't been invalidated. Saves 2 bytes per ebp-relative match (3-byte push-mem → 1-byte push-reg), 4-5 bytes for label/SIB-form memory.
  - **Common shape**: for-loop body where the cmp at the top loaded the loop counter into EAX, then a function-call arg push re-reads the same memory. After my pass: `push eax` directly. Concrete win on `_sum_squares` (sums squares of [0, n)): per-iteration loop body's `push dword [ebp - 8]` becomes `push eax` (saves 2 bytes per call site).
  - **Differs from `push_memory`** (which collapses ADJACENT `mov reg, [m]; push reg` to `push dword [m]` when reg is dead — saves 1 byte by dropping the 3-byte mov, gaining only the size prefix). My pass goes the OTHER direction: when load and push are NON-adjacent (separated by intermediate code that uses REG), keeping REG and using `push REG` is shorter than the explicit memory push.
  - **Tracking model**: per-register `reg_mem` map updated as the pass walks lines. Set on `mov REG, [m]` (for ebp-rel or label memory), invalidated by any write to REG, by writes to overlapping memory, by labels (control-flow boundaries), jumps/calls (caller-saved-reg clobber, control flow), directives/data (function boundary), or implicit-reg-touching ops (cdq/idiv/etc.).
  - **Conservative aliasing**: any memory write invalidates all tracking (no alias analysis). SIB-form memory operands (containing `*`) are excluded from tracking.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests. 1065 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: lea_sib_label_load_collapse**: collapse `lea REG, [LABEL + REG*scale (+ DISP_A)?]; <op> ..., [REG (+ DISP_B)?]` (or vice versa for stores) into a single op with the SIB form directly: `<op> ..., [LABEL + REG*scale + (DISP_A + DISP_B)]`. Drops the 6+ byte LEA. Saves 6+ bytes per match.
  - **Common shape**: `if (g[i] == target)` and similar patterns where the codegen materializes the address of `g[i]` with `lea REG, [_g + REG*4]` then accesses via `[REG]`. After my pass: `cmp dword [_g + REG*4], target` directly.
  - **Supported B ops**: mov (load), cmp, test, add, sub, and, or, xor, inc, dec (RMW), push (deref). Both single-operand (push, inc, dec) and 2-operand forms work.
  - **Conditions**: A is `lea REG, [SIB-form involving REG]` where the source contains REG itself with scale ∈ {1, 2, 4, 8}; B's memory operand is `[REG (+ M)?]` (no SIB on B); REG dead after B (`treat_as_scratch=True`) or REG == DST of B's load.
  - **Concrete win on `_find` (linear search)**: `lea eax, [_g + eax*4]; cmp dword [eax], edx; jne .L_skip; mov eax, [ebp - 4]; jmp .epilogue` cascades through to `cmp dword [_g + eax*4], edx; je .epilogue`. Saves 4+ instructions per qualifying loop iteration.
  - **Cascades** with `jcc_jmp_inversion` and `redundant_eax_load` to drop the redundant `mov eax, [ebp - 4]; jmp .epilogue` (since EAX already holds [ebp - 4]'s value at the je point).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +7 peephole tests. 1072 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: dup_load_to_copy**: collapse adjacent same-memory loads. Pattern `mov R1, [m]; mov R2, [m]` → `mov R1, [m]; mov R2, R1`. Saves bytes for any non-trivial memory operand:
  - ebp-rel `[ebp ± N]` (3-4 bytes): saves 1-2 bytes
  - label `[_glob]` (5+ bytes): saves 3+ bytes
  - SIB form `[_g + reg*4]` (7+ bytes): saves 5+ bytes
  - **Common after `lea_sib_label_load_collapse`** produces two adjacent same-memory loads, e.g. for expressions like `g[i] + g[i]` or `pts[i].x; pts[i].y` patterns where the codegen evaluates each operand independently without memoization.
  - **Safety**: pass requires the memory operand to NOT reference R1 (else after A modifies R1, B's address would be different). Memory operands are compared textually after stripping size prefixes and normalizing whitespace.
  - **Sister of `dup_load_chain_to_copy`** which handles the 4-line `mov R1, [m]; mov R1, [R1+N1]; mov R2, [m]; mov R2, [R2+N2]` chained-deref pattern. My pass handles the simpler 2-line case where the loads aren't followed by a chain.

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +6 peephole tests. 1078 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: dead_unused_slot_stores**: drop `mov [ebp ± N], SRC` stores to slots that are never read or address-taken anywhere in the function. Saves 3+ bytes per dropped store.
  - **Per-function analysis**: identify each slot N where there's no read reference (`mov reg, [ebp - N]`, `cmp reg, [ebp - N]`, `push dword [ebp - N]`, etc.), no `lea reg, [ebp - N]` (address-taken would let reads happen indirectly), and no RMW (`add [ebp - N], X`, `inc dword [ebp - N]`, etc.). Then drop all `mov [ebp ± N], SRC` (pure overwrite stores) to that slot.
  - **Pre-conditions per function**: function must have `enter` or `push ebp` prologue (skip synthetic test asm fragments). Bail if any `lea reg, [ebp ± N]` or `mov reg, ebp` (stack frame potentially address-taken). Bail if any SIB-form `[ebp + idx*K (+ N)]` access (runtime-variable index could read any slot).
  - **Bug found during integration: SIB-form ebp-access detection**. The first version of the pass only recognized literal `[ebp ± N]` as slot references — but `int a[8] = {0..7}` inside a function that reads `a[i]` via `[ebp + ecx*4 - 32]` (SIB form) wasn't detected as reading the array slots, so my pass dropped all the array initializers. Caught by torture's `20030105-1` and `mode-dependent-address`. Fixed by adding a regex pre-pass that finds any `[*ebp*]` bracket and rejects it if the inner doesn't match the safe form `\s*ebp\s*([+-]\s*\d+)?\s*`. Any non-literal use of `ebp` inside a memory operand (SIB-form, register-base, anything) bails the entire function.
  - **Common shape**: a function with `int d = ...; if (cond) d = -d; return d;` where the codegen stores `d` to a frame slot for completeness but the value flows through EAX. The codegen doesn't currently do this dead-store elimination, so peephole picks it up.
  - **Concrete win**: `_abs_diff` (probe) saves 6 bytes by dropping 2 dead stores. 30 c-testsuite files have 53 total fires (~159 bytes saved across c-testsuite).

  **Result: 1514/1514 gcc-c-torture (--full), 220/220 c-testsuite (--full) still 100%**. +9 peephole tests. 1107 unit tests total. Pipeline 1734/1734 (100%).
- **2026-04-30 — Phase A peephole: dup_addr_compute_collapse**: drop a 4-line address-recompute when an immediately-preceding 3-line compute produced the same address, separated by a deref that doesn't clobber the address-holding register.
  - **Pattern (9 consecutive instr lines)**:
    - A: `mov R1, MEM1` (load base)
    - C: `imul R2, R2, K` or `shl R2, N` (scale; R2 already held the index)
    - D: `add R1, R2` (R1 = &elem)
    - E: `mov R3, [R1 + off1]` (first deref, R3 != R1, R3 != R2)
    - F: `mov R1, MEM1` (= A; drop)
    - G: `mov R2, MEM2` (drop)
    - H: `imul R2, R2, K` (= C; drop)
    - I: `add R1, R2` (= D; drop)
    - J: `mov R4, [R1 + off2]` (second deref)
  - **Why this works**: After E, R1 still holds &elem (since R3 != R1). After dropping F-I, R1 unchanged; J's deref via [R1 + off2] correctly accesses the second member.
  - **Pre-value verification**: For correctness, R2's value before A must equal what G loads. Verified by scanning backward within the same basic block from A: the most recent write to R2 must be a `mov R2, MEM_Y` that textually matches G's source. Bails on any other write to R2 (RMW, implicit-reg-writer, function call, etc.).
